<p><b>Cambrai</b> (<small>French pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[kɑ̃bʁɛ]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Fr-Paris--Cambrai.ogg" title="File:Fr-Paris--Cambrai.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/03/Fr-Paris--Cambrai.ogg" title="Fr-Paris--Cambrai.ogg">listen</a>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Picard_language" title="Picard language">Picard</a>: <span lang="pcd" xml:lang="pcd"><i>Kimbré</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl"><i>Kamerijk</i></span>; old spelling <i>Cambray</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">commune</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Nord_(French_department)" title="Nord (French department)">Nord</a> <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">department</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Hauts-de-France" title="Hauts-de-France">Hauts-de-France</a> <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_France" title="Regions of France">region</a> of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> river, which is known locally as the Escaut river.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Subprefectures_in_France" title="Subprefectures in France">sub-prefecture</a> of the department, Cambrai is a town which had 32,518 inhabitants in the Census of 2009. It is in the heart of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Urban_unit_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Urban unit of Cambrai (page does not exist)">urban unit of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit%C3%A9_urbaine_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Unité urbaine de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span> which, with 47,138 inhabitants, ranks as 7th largest of the department. Its <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Urban_area_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Urban area of Cambrai (page does not exist)">urban area</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aire_urbaine_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Aire urbaine de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, a more extensive range, included 65,986 inhabitants in 2009. With <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a> and the towns of the former <a href="/wiki/Nord-Pas_de_Calais_Mining_Basin" title="Nord-Pas de Calais Mining Basin">Nord-Pas de Calais Mining Basin</a>, it is also part of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_area_of_Lille&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Metropolitan area of Lille (page does not exist)">Metropolitan area of Lille</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aire_m%C3%A9tropolitaine_de_Lille" title="fr:Aire métropolitaine de Lille">fr</a>)</span> which has more than 3.8 million inhabitants.</p>
<p>Towards the end of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, Cambrai replaced <a href="/wiki/Bavay" title="Bavay">Bavay</a> as the "capital" of the land of the <a href="/wiki/Nervii" title="Nervii">Nervii</a>. At the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Merovingian_dynasty" title="Merovingian dynasty">Merovingian</a> era, Cambrai became the seat of an immense <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Cambrai" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cambrai">archdiocese</a> covering all the right bank of the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> and the centre of a small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_principality" title="Ecclesiastical principality">ecclesiastical principality</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principaut%C3%A9_eccl%C3%A9siastique" title="fr:Principauté ecclésiastique">fr</a>)</span>, roughly coinciding with the shire of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a>, including the central part of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>. The bishopric had some limited secular power and depended on the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> until annexation to France in 1678. <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_F%C3%A9nelon" title="François Fénelon">Fénelon</a>, nicknamed the "Swan of Cambrai", was the most renowned of the archbishops.</p>
<p>The fertile lands which surround it and the textile industry gave it prosperity in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, but in modern times it is less industrialised than its neighbours of <a href="/wiki/Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="Nord-Pas-de-Calais">Nord-Pas-de-Calais</a>.</p>
<p>Cambrai was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Wellington" title="Duke of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a>'s headquarters, for the British Army of Occupation, from 1815 to 1818. Occupied and partly destroyed by the German army during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Cambrai saw unfold in its vicinity the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1917)" title="Battle of Cambrai (1917)">Battle of Cambrai</a> (20 November 1917 – 3 December 1917) where <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tanks</a> were massively and successfully used for the first time. A second <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1918)" title="Battle of Cambrai (1918)">Battle of Cambrai</a> took place between 8 and 10 October 1918 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days_Offensive" title="Hundred Days Offensive">Hundred Days Offensive</a>. <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> was followed by reconstructions and a rapidly developing economy and population, abruptly reversed by the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>.</p>
<p>Cambrai today is a lively city and, despite the past destruction, maintains a rich monumental heritage. Cambrai is affirmed as the urban centre of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Cambrésis">Cambrésis</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="fr:Cambrésis">fr</a>)</span>. Its economic life is strengthened by its position on the main local highway and river.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai-Position.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="234" data-file-width="295" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cambrai-Position.png/220px-Cambrai-Position.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c9/Cambrai-Position.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai-Position.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geographic situation of Cambrai in the Nord department</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The town of Cambrai is located in the south of the Nord Department, of which it is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chef-lieu" title="Chef-lieu">chef-lieu</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement" title="Arrondissement">arrondissement</a>. It belongs to the dense network of the cities of the area which are separated by a few tens of kilometres: <a href="/wiki/Douai" title="Douai">Douai</a> is only 24 kilometres (15 mi), <a href="/wiki/Valenciennes" title="Valenciennes">Valenciennes</a> is 29 kilometres (18 mi), <a href="/wiki/Arras" title="Arras">Arras</a> is 36 kilometres (22 mi) and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Quentin,_Aisne" title="Saint-Quentin, Aisne">Saint-Quentin</a> 37 kilometres (23 mi) <a href="/wiki/As_the_crow_flies" title="As the crow flies">as the crow flies</a>. The regional capital of <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a> is 52 kilometres (32 mi) away.</p>
<p>Cambrai is not very far from several European capitals: <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> is 108 kilometres (67 mi), <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> is 160 kilometres (99 mi) and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> is 280 kilometres (170 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city was born and developed on the right bank of the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> river. Locally known as the Escaut, the river has its source in the department of <a href="/wiki/Aisne" title="Aisne">Aisne</a>, which is barely any more than 20 kilometres (12 mi) away.</p>

</div>

<td nowrap="nowrap" style="width:0%; text-align: center">  <b>Cambrai</b>  </td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_landforms">Geology and landforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geology and landforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="386" data-file-width="600" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png/220px-NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png/330px-NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png/440px-NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NPdC_relief_Cambrai.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cambrai in its topographical context</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai is located on <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a> bedrock of the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> period, which forms the northern boundary of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Basin" title="Paris Basin">Paris Basin</a>, between, to the east, the hills for <a href="/wiki/Thi%C3%A9rache" title="Thiérache">Thiérache</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement_of_Avesnes-sur-Helpe" title="Arrondissement of Avesnes-sur-Helpe">Avesnois</a>, the foothills of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Massif_ardennais&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Massif ardennais (page does not exist)">Ardennes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massif_ardennais" title="fr:Massif ardennais">fr</a>)</span>, and northwest, the hills of <a href="/wiki/Artois" title="Artois">Artois</a>. It is at a point which is relatively lower than these two regions, called the "Cambrai threshold" or the "Bapaume threshold", which facilitates the passage between the south and the north: Bapaume (Artois) is 100 metres (330 ft) above sea level, <a href="/wiki/Avesnes-sur-Helpe" title="Avesnes-sur-Helpe">Avesnes-sur-Helpe</a> (Avesnois) is at 143 metres (469 ft) and Cambrai only 41 metres (135 ft). The <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_Saint-Quentin" title="Canal de Saint-Quentin">Saint-Quentin canal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canal_du_Nord" title="Canal du Nord">Canal du Nord</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A1_autoroute_(France)" title="A1 autoroute (France)">A1</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A2_autoroute_(France)" title="A2 autoroute (France)">A2</a> and <a href="/wiki/A26_autoroute" title="A26 autoroute">A26</a> autoroutes all borrow all this passage between the basin of the <a href="/wiki/Seine" title="Seine">Seine</a> and the plains of the Nord department.</p>
<p>The chalky subsoil allowed, as in many medieval cities, the digging of a network of cellars, tunnels and quarries under the city. The poor quality of the Cambrai chalk was reserved for use in the manufacture of lime or filling, as well as common constructions. For prestigious buildings, stone from the nearby villages of <a href="/wiki/Noyelles-sur-Escaut" title="Noyelles-sur-Escaut">Noyelles-sur-Escaut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rumilly-en-Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Rumilly-en-Cambrésis">Rumilly</a> or <a href="/wiki/Marcoing" title="Marcoing">Marcoing</a> was used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[a 1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is bordered in its western part, as well as to the north and the south, by the alluvial zones of the Scheldt Valley.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hydrography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG/220px-Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG/330px-Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG/440px-Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tour_des_Arquets_Cambrai_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Tower of Arquets (14th century) controlled the entry of the Scheldt in the city and the flood defences</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai is built on the right bank of the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a>. The river, still of a very modest flow in Cambrai,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup> played a crucial role in the history of the city by providing multiple functions, including allowing the transportation of men and goods since antiquity. However, it was undeveloped and was crossed by numerous marshes. It was with the discovery of coal at <a href="/wiki/Anzin" title="Anzin">Anzin</a> in 1734 that the Scheldt was expanded and declared navigable in 1780, from Cambrai to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[a 2]</a></sup> The Scheldt is today the <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_l%27Escaut" title="Canal de l'Escaut">Canal de l'Escaut</a> downstream of Cambrai.</p>
<p>In addition, the river initially served as the boundary between the bishoprics of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Tournai" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Tournai">Tournai</a> on its left bank and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Cambrai" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cambrai">Cambrai</a> on its right bank, from the 6th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[c 1]</a></sup> When the division of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>'s Empire in 843, this border was retained to delimit the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Lothair_I" title="Lothair I">Lothair I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bald" title="Charles the Bald">Charles the Bald</a>, making Cambrai a city of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> until 1677.</p>
<p>The Scheldt was also indispensable to many economic activities, such as the tanning, milling, the manufacture of salt and soap,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[a 3]</a></sup> as well as for <a href="/wiki/Retting" title="Retting">retting</a> of <a href="/wiki/Linen" title="Linen">linen</a>, the weaving of which was one of the main activities of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[b 1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally, the river was used in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and then by <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Le_Prestre_de_Vauban" title="Sébastien Le Prestre de Vauban">Vauban</a>, for the defence of the city by the establishment of flood defensive areas.</p>
<p>Despite its important role in the history of the city, the Scheldt is little integrated into the present urban landscape.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dd>Main article: <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_of_Nord-Pas-de-Calais&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Climate of Nord-Pas-de-Calais (page does not exist)">Climate of Nord-Pas-de-Calais</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climat_du_Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="fr:Climat du Nord-Pas-de-Calais">fr</a>)</span></i></dd>
</dl>
<p>Climate in this area has mild differences between highs and lows, and there is adequate rainfall year round. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Classification" title="Köppen Climate Classification">Köppen Climate Classification</a> subtype for this climate is "<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification#GROUP_C:_Mild_Temperate.2Fmesothermal_climates" title="Köppen climate classification">Cfb</a>" (Marine West Coast Climate/<a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[3]</a></sup> However, the city is about 110 kilometres (68 mi) from the nearest coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[note 1]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">Precipitation</a> is distributed year-round, with highs in the spring and autumn, with February being the driest month. Contrasting with the rainy image of the region, the total annual precipitation is relatively small with 642 millimetres (25.3 in) at Cambrai-Épinoy; identical to the Montsouris Paris station, which is at the same altitude, it is less than those of <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> at 656 millimetres (25.8 in) or <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> at 767 millimetres (30.2 in). However, the number of days of rain (63 in Nice, 120 in Cambrai) confirms the oceanic character of the climate.</p>
<p>The mean <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_temperature_range" title="Atmospheric temperature range">thermal amplitude</a> between the winter and summer does not exceed 15 °C. Although again establishing a comparison with Paris, that Cambrai is 1.5 to 2 °C colder over all combined seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[4]</a></sup> On average, there are 71 days of fog per year (Paris-Montsouris has 13) 15 days of storm (Paris-Montsouris has 19) and 20 days with snow (Paris-Montsouris has 15).</p>
<p>If comparing the data of Cambrai and those of towns such as <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a> or <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[5]</a></sup> there are colder minimum temperatures and a warmer maximum in Cambrai, the difference being approximately 2 °C, as well as a larger number of freezing days and less heavy precipitation: It's said a "transitional" oceanic climate, with some continental influences.</p>
<p>The temperature record in Cambrai is 38.2 °C (100.8 °F), which was established on 6 August 2003<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[6]</a></sup> (data collected since 1954 and record updated to 5 September 2013).</p>
