<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Routes_of_communication_and_transport">Routes of communication and transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Routes of communication and transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:French_A26_motorway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/French_A26_motorway.jpg/220px-French_A26_motorway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/French_A26_motorway.jpg/330px-French_A26_motorway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/French_A26_motorway.jpg/440px-French_A26_motorway.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:French_A26_motorway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The A26 autoroute at its intersection with the A2, near Cambrai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai is located at the crossroads of two French autoroutes, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A2_autoroute_(France)" title="A2 autoroute (France)">A2</a> from <a href="/wiki/Combles" title="Combles">Combles</a> (junction with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A1_autoroute_(France)" title="A1 autoroute (France)">A1</a> coming from Paris) to the Franco-Belgian border, opened in 1973, and the <a href="/wiki/A26_autoroute" title="A26 autoroute">A26</a> from <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> to <a href="/wiki/Troyes" title="Troyes">Troyes</a>, opened in 1992. These autoroutes partly merge with the <a href="/wiki/International_E-road_network" title="International E-road network">European roads</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E19" title="European route E19">E19</a> from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> via <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, for the A2, and the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E17" title="European route E17">E17</a> from <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> to <a href="/wiki/Beaune" title="Beaune">Beaune</a> via <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a>, for the A26.</p>
<p>Cambrai and its region are served by four autoroute interchanges: The A2, exit 14 (Cambrai) from <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> and exit 15 (<a href="/wiki/Bouchain" title="Bouchain">Bouchain</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, and on the A26 the exits 8 (<a href="/wiki/Marquion" title="Marquion">Marquion</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> and 9 (<a href="/wiki/Masni%C3%A8res" title="Masnières">Masnières</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a>.</p>
<p>Cambrai is also at the crossroads of the <a href="/wiki/Route_nationale_30" title="Route nationale 30">Route nationale 30</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bapaume" title="Bapaume">Bapaume</a> to <a href="/wiki/Qui%C3%A9vrain" title="Quiévrain">Quiévrain</a> (Franco-Belgian border), <a href="/wiki/Route_nationale_43" title="Route nationale 43">Route nationale 43</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Ruffine" title="Sainte-Ruffine">Sainte-Ruffine</a> (<a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Route_nationale_44&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Route nationale 44 (page does not exist)">Route nationale 44</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_nationale_44_(France)" title="fr:Route nationale 44 (France)">fr</a>)</span> of Cambrai to <a href="/wiki/Vitry-le-Fran%C3%A7ois" title="Vitry-le-François">Vitry</a> (these last three have since 2006 been downgraded to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=French_departmental_road_network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="French departmental road network (page does not exist)">departmental roads</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_routier_d%C3%A9partemental_fran%C3%A7ais" title="fr:Réseau routier départemental français">fr</a>)</span> and therefore consequently renamed to D6xx), and D939 (former <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Route_nationale_39&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Route nationale 39 (page does not exist)">Route nationale 39</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_nationale_39_(France)" title="fr:Route nationale 39 (France)">fr</a>)</span>) of Cambrai to <a href="/wiki/Arras" title="Arras">Arras</a>.</p>
<p>To facilitate access to the east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Cambrésis">Cambrésis</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="fr:Cambrésis">fr</a>)</span> from the A2 and A26 autoroutes, to alleviate traffic in the crossing of the city and to serve the future Niergnies business zone, a southern bypass was the subject of a <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9claration_d%27utilit%C3%A9_publique" title="Déclaration d'utilité publique">declaration of public utility</a> (DPU) on 22 April 1999. Its route has been repeatedly modified and challenged, because it crosses the urban ecological park of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Regional_Natural_Reserve_of_the_River_Escaut&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Regional Natural Reserve of the River Escaut (page does not exist)">Chenu Wood</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9serve_naturelle_r%C3%A9gionale_de_l%27Escaut-rivi%C3%A8re" title="fr:Réserve naturelle régionale de l'Escaut-rivière">fr</a>)</span> in <a href="/wiki/Proville" title="Proville">Proville</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[9]</a></sup> the only public natural green space of the Cambrésis. The bypass is in service since 17 September 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VdNContSud_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-VdNContSud-16">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>A bypass to the north is also part of the program of major departmental projects, which was required to have been initiated by 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VdNContSud_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-VdNContSud-16">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The SNCF railway station in Cambrai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Cambrai" title="Gare de Cambrai">Cambrai railway station</a> is connected by direct trains (<a href="/wiki/TER_Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="TER Nord-Pas-de-Calais">TER</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douai" title="Douai">Douai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valenciennes" title="Valenciennes">Valenciennes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Quentin,_Aisne" title="Saint-Quentin, Aisne">Saint-Quentin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a>.</p>
<p>The link to Douai and Lille has improved after the electrification of the single-track <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Saint-Just-en-Chauss%C3%A9e_to_Douai_railway_line&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Saint-Just-en-Chaussée to Douai railway line (page does not exist)">Douai to Cambrai line</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ligne_de_Saint-Just-en-Chauss%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Douai" title="fr:Ligne de Saint-Just-en-Chaussée à Douai">fr</a>)</span> in 1993, for the commissioning of joining <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> to Cambrai by <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> via Douai, which was subsequently cancelled. Direct connections on weekdays are fifteen trains per day, with a journey time of about 30 minutes between Douai and Cambrai; eight trains, with a journey time often less than an hour, to <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Lille_Flandres" title="Gare de Lille Flandres">Lille-Flandres station</a>; ten trains, with a time of little more than 40 minutes on average to Valenciennes and a dozen trains, with a journey time of around 50 minutes, to Saint-Quentin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sncf_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-sncf-17">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambrai is directly connected by rail to any European city, but links to Paris (<a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a>) are mediocre if compared to those of the neighbouring cities. Valenciennes, Douai and Arras are connected to Paris by TGV several times per day. Saint-Quentin is connected by TER or <a href="/wiki/Intercit%C3%A9s" title="Intercités">Intercités</a> trains with less than two hours travel time. Cambrai was connected to Paris in 2010 by a single direct Intercités service of two hours, with a little-suited schedule for professional use. The times of other trains via Douai or Saint-Quentin vary between two and four and a half hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_history">Railway history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Railway history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="521" data-file-width="832" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg/220px-Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg/330px-Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg/440px-Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Cambrai_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gare_de_Cambrai-Annexe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gare de Cambrai-Annexe (page does not exist)">Gare de Cambrai-Annexe</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gare_de_Cambrai-Annexe" title="fr:Gare de Cambrai-Annexe">fr</a>)</span> in 1913</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="528" data-file-width="818" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg/220px-Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg/330px-Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg/440px-Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gare_cambr%C3%A9sis_cambrai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Gare du Cambrésis, former head of the line of the <a href="/wiki/Chemin_de_Fer_du_Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Chemin de Fer du Cambrésis">Chemin de Fer du Cambrésis</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_de_plaisance_Cantimpr%C3%A9_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The marina of Cantimpré</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As early as 1833 the municipal council sought passage of a railway line through Cambrai. However, a route through Arras and Douai, to Lille, with a branch to Valenciennes, was preferred in 1845. It remained, therefore, to connect Cambrai to this line, which was done in 1878 by a single, winding line between Cambrai and Douai. Meanwhile Cambrai had been linked, in 1858, to the Paris-Brussels line by a branch line from <a href="/wiki/Busigny" title="Busigny">Busigny</a> and joining <a href="/wiki/Somain,_Nord" title="Somain, Nord">Somain</a>, near Douai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[c 2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other railway lines of <a href="/wiki/Voie_ferr%C3%A9e_d%27int%C3%A9r%C3%AAt_local" title="Voie ferrée d'intérêt local">local interest</a> saw development in the 19th century, particularly in 1880 the <a href="/wiki/Chemin_de_Fer_du_Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Chemin de Fer du Cambrésis">Société des Chemin de Fer du Cambrésis</a> which operated three routes in the Cambrésis between Cambrai, Caudry, Saint-Quentin, Le Cateau and Denain. An agricultural use of Cambrai to Marquion, now off line, was also open in 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[a 4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambrai railway station was also the terminus of a standard gauge secondary route of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Compagnie_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_de_voies_ferr%C3%A9es_d%27int%C3%A9r%C3%AAt_local&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Compagnie générale de voies ferrées d'intérêt local (page does not exist)">CGL/VFIL</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compagnie_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_de_voies_ferr%C3%A9es_d%27int%C3%A9r%C3%AAt_local" title="fr:Compagnie générale de voies ferrées d'intérêt local">fr</a>)</span> linking <a href="/wiki/Marquion" title="Marquion">Marquion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boisleux-au-Mont" title="Boisleux-au-Mont">Boisleux-au-Mont</a>.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_projects">Railway projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Railway projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The regional transport scheme evokes three axes or projects concerning Cambrai: Improving the Douai-Cambrai connections, the construction of a new railway line between Cambrai and <a href="/wiki/Marquion" title="Marquion">Marquion</a>-<a href="/wiki/Arras" title="Arras">Arras</a>, in conjunction with the large gauge <a href="/wiki/Seine%E2%80%93Nord_Europe_Canal" title="Seine–Nord Europe Canal">Seine-North Europe canal</a> project and the establishment of a business zone of Marquion, as well as "searching for a link from <a href="/wiki/Orchies" title="Orchies">Orchies</a> towards Cambrai".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">Waterways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Waterways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cambrai is one of the seven territorial subdivisions of the regional management of Nord-Pas-de-Calais of <a href="/wiki/Voies_navigables_de_France" title="Voies navigables de France">navigable waterways in France</a>. The city is located at the junction of the <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_Saint-Quentin" title="Canal de Saint-Quentin">Saint-Quentin canal</a> to the Oise and Paris and the <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_l%27Escaut" title="Canal de l'Escaut">Canal de l'Escaut</a>, which leads to the <a href="/wiki/Canal_Dunkerque-Escaut" title="Canal Dunkerque-Escaut">Dunkerque-Escaut canal</a>. Commercial traffic on these canals is low, of the order of 250,000 tonnes upstream of Cambrai and 420,000 tonnes downstream.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Marina" title="Marina">marina</a> is located at the junction of the two canals, at Cambrai-Cantimpré.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways_history">Waterways history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Waterways history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_l%27Escaut" title="Canal de l'Escaut">Canal de l'Escaut</a> (<a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> canal), between Cambrai and <a href="/wiki/Valenciennes" title="Valenciennes">Valenciennes</a>, was opened to navigation in 1780.</p>
<p>Moreover a river link between Paris and the Nord department had been projected as early as the time of <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Mazarin" title="Cardinal Mazarin">Mazarin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Colbert" title="Jean-Baptiste Colbert">Colbert</a>. The construction of the <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_Saint-Quentin" title="Canal de Saint-Quentin">Saint-Quentin canal</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Chauny" title="Chauny">Chauny</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Oise_(river)" title="Oise (river)">Oise</a> and Cambrai, was taken up in 1802 on the order of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon I</a> and completed in 1810, after the drilling of the <a href="/wiki/Riqueval_Tunnel" title="Riqueval Tunnel">Riqueval Tunnel</a>. The canal and tunnel were opened with great pomp on 28 April 1810 by the Emperor and Empress <a href="/wiki/Marie_Louise,_Duchess_of_Parma" title="Marie Louise, Duchess of Parma">Marie-Louise</a>. The Saint-Quentin canal has experienced heavy traffic, but since 1966, the date of the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Canal_du_Nord" title="Canal du Nord">Canal du Nord</a>, it has lost much of its importance.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways_projects">Waterways projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Waterways projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>A wide-gauge river link project, called <a href="/wiki/Seine%E2%80%93Nord_Europe_Canal" title="Seine–Nord Europe Canal">Seine-Escaut Link</a> project is part of the 30 priority projects of the future <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Transport_Networks" title="Trans-European Transport Networks">trans-European transport network</a>. The route of this project is through <a href="/wiki/Marquion" title="Marquion">Marquion</a>, 12 kilometres (7.5 mi) west of Cambrai. A platform of activities is planned therein. The commissioning of the canal could take place around 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cambrai is in close proximity to two airfields: <i>Cambrai-Epinoy</i>, to the north-west, whose use was booked at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Airbase_103_Cambrai-%C3%89pinoy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Airbase 103 Cambrai-Épinoy (page does not exist)">Airbase 103</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_a%C3%A9rienne_103_Cambrai-%C3%89pinoy" title="fr:Base aérienne 103 Cambrai-Épinoy">fr</a>)</span> until its closure in 2012, and <i><a href="/wiki/Cambrai-Niergnies_Airport" title="Cambrai-Niergnies Airport">Cambrai Niergnies</a></i>, 5 kilometres (3.1 mi) to the southeast, opened to recreational aviation.</p>
<p>Within an approximate radius of 1 hr 30 mins by road are five major airports: <a href="/wiki/Lille_Airport" title="Lille Airport">Lille-Lesquin</a> at 60 kilometres (37 mi), <a href="/wiki/Brussels_South_Charleroi_Airport" title="Brussels South Charleroi Airport">Brussels South Charleroi</a> at 114 kilometres (71 mi), <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels National</a> at 148 kilometres (92 mi), <a href="/wiki/Beauvais%E2%80%93Till%C3%A9_Airport" title="Beauvais–Tillé Airport">Paris Beauvais-Tillé</a> at 151 kilometres (94 mi) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris Charles-de-Gaulle</a> at 152 kilometres (94 mi).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_Transport">Urban Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Urban Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1045" data-file-width="1618" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG/220px-LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG/330px-LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG/440px-LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LL_67_-_CAMBRAI_-_La_Grand%27Place_-_Station_des_Tramways.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The tramway in 1905, in the main square</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle" role="note">Main articles: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tramway_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tramway of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Tramway of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tramway_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Tramway de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Public_transport_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Public transport of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Public transport of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transports_en_commun_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Transports en commun de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span></div>
<p>By 1897, that is, upon completion of the demolition of the fortifications, the city had considered the construction of electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a> lines. It was a very modern solution for the time, since electric traction only appeared in 1881 and the development of this mode of transport didn't truly occur until 1895 in Paris and the Paris region. In 1903, the network of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tramway_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tramway of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Compagnie des tramways de Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tramway_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Tramway de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span> was opened, 16 kilometres (9.9 mi)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[b 2]</a></sup> and with five lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[15]</a></sup> After World War I, the uneconomic network was not recommissioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[a 5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1933 the agglomeration of Cambrai has been served by a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Public_transport_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Public transport of Cambrai (page does not exist)">network of buses</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transports_en_commun_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Transports en commun de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, five urban routes were operating in 2010, run by CFC (Railways of Cambrésis):</p>
<ul>
<li>A: Luxembourg - Cambrai stations - <a href="/wiki/Escaud%C5%93uvres" title="Escaudœuvres">Escaudœuvres</a></li>
<li>B: <a href="/wiki/Neuville-Saint-R%C3%A9my" title="Neuville-Saint-Rémy">Neuville-Saint-Rémy</a> - Cambrai stations - ZAC Cambrai-South</li>
<li>C: Les Martigues-Pyrénées - Cambrai stations - <a href="/wiki/Raillencourt-Sainte-Olle" title="Raillencourt-Sainte-Olle">Raillencourt-Sainte-Olle</a></li>
<li>D: Cambrai stations - Raillencourt-Sainte-Olle</li>
<li>E: ZAC Cambrai-South - Cambrai stations</li>
</ul>
<p>Since 7 January 2013, the agglomeration community of Cambrai has implemented a free shuttle which serves seventeen stops around the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, the "Urban Transport Perimeter" (PTU) of Cambrai which, with 59,326 inhabitants, is the smallest of the twelve PTU of the <a href="/wiki/Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="Nord-Pas-de-Calais">Nord-Pas-de-Calais</a> region had completed about 400,000 kilometres (250,000 mi) per year, corresponding to 740,000 journeys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The agglomeration community of Cambrai is the organising authority of urban transport. However, while it has twenty-three communes, only six were served by urban transport in 2006. For other towns and cities, the urban community has delegated jurisdiction to the department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a relatively sparsely populated agglomeration with little extensive public transport, it cannot easily compete with the automobile. Nevertheless, the agglomeration community of Cambrai reflects on the future of urban transport from a perspective of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>, with aims to strengthen the supply of public transport in order to capture a portion of travel by private car, and reducing car traffic and CO<sub>2</sub> emissions. The realisation of the new multimodal transport hub in the quarter of the railway station of Cambrai is part of this policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanism">Urbanism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Urbanism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_morphology">Urban morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Urban morphology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The old centre of Cambrai was established on a small rise overlooking, from the right bank, the marshy area of the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> Valley. Indications suggest that a <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">castrum</a> was built at this location, although the scarcity of excavations at Cambrai in has provided no archaeological evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[b 3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[c 3]</a></sup> With its area of 4.4 hectares (11 acres), the very modest castrum would've been much smaller than those of <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne</a> at 13 hectares (32 acres) and <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a> at 56 hectares (140 acres), for example.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Faubourg" title="Faubourg">Faubourgs</a> were developed, at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Merovingian_dynasty" title="Merovingian dynasty">Merovingian</a> prosperity, to the north and west of the primitive castrum, around the churches of Saint-Vaast and Saint-Aubert. The looting of the city by the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> in December 880 convinced the Bishop Dodilon to strengthen and expand fortifications: The new enclosure he built tripled the size of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[b 4]</a></sup> To the southeast, on a hillock called Mont-des-Bœufs, Bishop <a href="/wiki/Gaugericus" title="Gaugericus">Gaugericus</a> had founded an abbey in 595, originally dedicated to Saint Médard and Saint Loup, then, after the death of the founder, Gaugericus himself. This abbey was certainly also protected by an enclosure. The space which separated these two urban cores hosted markets and fairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[b 5]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_(Atlas_van_Loon).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4405" data-file-width="5500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg/220px-Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg/330px-Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg/440px-Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_(Atlas_van_Loon).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
City map dating from 1649</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1884" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg/220px-Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg/330px-Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg/440px-Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of 1710</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>These two quarters were joined in the 11th century when Bishop <a href="/wiki/Gerard_of_Florennes" title="Gerard of Florennes">Gérard I</a> built the churches of Saint Nicolas and the <a href="/wiki/Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Cambrai Cathedral">Saint Sepulchre</a>, southeast of the city and east of Mont-des-Bœufs. The town hall, the market, butcher and various bodies of craftsmen settled in this new urban space that Bishop Lietbert had protected by an earth rampart. Even today the <i>Grand-place</i>, the covered market, and a few names of streets (the <i>Rue de Liniers</i>, <i>Rue des Rôtisseurs</i>, <i>Rue des Chaudronniers</i> and <i>Rue des Cordiers</i>) recall this stage of urban development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[b 6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bishop <a href="/wiki/Gerard_II_(bishop_of_Cambrai)" title="Gerard II (bishop of Cambrai)">Gérard II</a> later replaced the earth rampart with a stone wall with towers, gates and ditches and encompassed the entire built space. Therefore Cambrai had reached the perimeter it would retain until the 19th century: While other cities in the region such as <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a> or <a href="/wiki/Douai" title="Douai">Douai</a> expanded their enclosures until the 14th century, that of Cambrai was redesigned and reinforced, but without affecting the outline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[b 7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[d 1]</a></sup> The outline of this wall from the 11th century is still visible in the current boulevards.</p>
<p>It was probably under the episcopates of the bishops Gérard I, Liebert and Gérard II, in the 11th century, that was built the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Château de Selles (page does not exist)">Château de Selles</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles" title="fr:Château de Selles">fr</a>)</span>, a fortress located on the edge of the Scheldt to the northwest of the city. In the 13th century, the Bishop Nicolas III de Fontaines ordered work to put it "on a good foot of defence".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[20]</a></sup> This castle, owned by the bishop-counts, was intended as much to monitor the city as to ensure the defence. Its military role ended in the 16th century, when <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> grabbed the city and ordered the construction, on Mont-des-Bœufs northeast of the town, of a citadel for which 800 houses were demolished along with the Abbey of Saint Gaugericus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[b 8]</a></sup> The Château de Selles was then used as a prison.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dismantling_of_fortifications">Dismantling of fortifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Dismantling of fortifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the 19th century the city was cramped within its fortified walls, which limited its development and prohibited any urban planning.</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Cambrai is one of the most inaccessible cities imaginable; its fortifications have a formidable appearance when it follows covered paths narrow and tortuous, crossing ditches filled by the Scheldt. Walls of extraordinary height enclose. The entrances, similar to tunnels, and barely sufficient for a car, lead to the city. All this overseen by a very daunting citadel built on top of Mont Saint-Géry.</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; text-align: right;"><cite>— <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Victor-Eug%C3%A8ne_Ardouin-Dumazet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Victor-Eugène Ardouin-Dumazet (page does not exist)">Ardouin-Dumazet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victor-Eug%C3%A8ne_Ardouin-Dumazet" title="fr:Victor-Eugène Ardouin-Dumazet">fr</a>)</span>, written in 1890.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[a 6]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The dismantling of the fortifications, requested by petition as early as 1862, was finally accepted by the State after a further 30 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[b 9]</a></sup> The work lasted 6 years and transformed the appearance of the city by the construction of a belt of wide <a href="/wiki/Boulevard" title="Boulevard">boulevards</a>, the sale of new land to build, connecting the city to its suburbs and the establishment of public gardens.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drainage_work">Drainage work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Drainage work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="811" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg/220px-Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg/330px-Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg/440px-Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_CPA_porte_des_arquets_escaut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entry of the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> into the city through the gate of Arquets (postcard from the early 20th century)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai is built on the edge of the wide marshy area of the Scheldt Valley encircling the western part of the city, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Château de Selles (page does not exist)">Château de Selles</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles" title="fr:Château de Selles">fr</a>)</span> to the north at the gate of the Holy Sepulchre in the south: Wet gardens, ponds, meadows, ponds and marsh formed a flood zone sometimes also used for the defence of the city. The suburb of Cantimpré, linking the ancient heart to the Scheldt below to the west, had raised several metres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[a 7]</a></sup> The two arms of the Scheldt (Escaut), the Escautins, are separated before entering the medieval town: The Escauette and the Clicotiau, which bathed the walls of the old urban core. These streams were probably due to man's hand because they do not correspond to natural landforms. However, it is unknown whether their origin dates back to the Roman era or is from a later time.</p>
<p>Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, and again in modern times, the Scheldt and its arms required constant work: Repair of levees, enhancement of pavement, straightening of the bed, as well as the digging of ditches to regulate the course of the river, prevent floods and ensure as far as possible a steady water level, on which the mills and tanneries depended. Despite these works, floods were frequent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[a 8]</a></sup> The absorption of rainwater and household water descending from the upper areas of the city was also a problem. Bouly spoke in 1842, in his <i>History of Cambrai and le Cambrésis</i>, of "fast torrents [stormwater] formed today by rolling up the Scheldt".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[21]</a></sup> In the Middle Ages the "flow of el kayère" (or "flow of the chair"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[note 2]</a></sup> close to the current <i>Grand-Place</i>, was dug a reservoir for "water courses of the falling waters of the sky", i.e. to control the flow of rainwater. In the 19th century aqueducts were built to carry these waters, and the streets were paved. Furthermore, in 1926 a drainage sewer was built at <i>Rue Blériot</i>.</p>
<p>The draining of the wetlands that surround the town began in 1804. The work ended in 1951 with the drying of the small stream of Saint Benoît near the Liberty Stadium, itself built on this wetland which dominated the ancient city walls, and in 1953 with the covering of the Clicotiau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[a 9]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_20th_century">The 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: The 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG/220px-Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG/330px-Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG/440px-Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_grand-place_maison_a_pignon.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
On the Grand-Place the specification of reconstruction imposed a regional style</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1049" data-file-width="1638" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG/220px-MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG/330px-MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG/440px-MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MERESSE_2038_-_CAMBRAI_Pendant_l%27incendie_-_La_Choque_et_Place_au_Bois.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of the town centre, in 1917</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The destruction caused by <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> necessitated a reconstruction of the centre. The municipality organised a competition, which was won by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Leprince-Ringuet (page does not exist)">Pierre Leprince-Ringuet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet" title="fr:Pierre Leprince-Ringuet">fr</a>)</span>. His project, inspired with both a <a href="/wiki/Regionalism_(politics)" title="Regionalism (politics)">regionalist</a> taste and the <a href="/wiki/Georges-Eug%C3%A8ne_Haussmann" title="Georges-Eugène Haussmann">Hausmannian</a> style, completely redesigned the layout of roads from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. It was rebuilt as a modern city. The architect <a href="/wiki/Louis_Marie_Cordonnier" title="Louis Marie Cordonnier">Louis Marie Cordonnier</a> described the prospects to elected representatives:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The centre of the city is completely razed and destroyed. So, you have free rein. Your duty is to remake a city pleasant, modern, retaining its character. Acting otherwise would be a crime for which you would be responsible to future generations. Your streets were narrow, twisty: Straighten them, adjust them, expand them. Your houses were awkward, obscure, unhealthy: Enforce in your specifications the requirementsfor hygiene, for ventilation, for lighting.</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; text-align: right;"><cite>— <a href="/wiki/Louis_Marie_Cordonnier" title="Louis Marie Cordonnier">Louis Marie Cordonnier</a>, <i>La Vie des Cambrésiens</i> [The Life of the People of Cambrai]<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[a 10]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The Leprince-Ringuet plan was only partially achieved, but the streets were removed, others expanded, and new paths were created as the <i>Avenue de la Victoire</i> [Avenue of Victory].</p>
<p>Further destruction due to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> bombing of April–August 1944 again required a reconstruction. It was especially, in the years following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, to rehouse the victims and to cope with the expanding population. Priority was given to detached houses, and new quarters appeared, such as the "Martin-Martine" subdivision south-east of the city. In the 1980s the municipality worked to restore and develop the ancient heritage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambrai had 16,256 housing units in 2007, of which 14,745 were occupied as primary residences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEE_logement_2007_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE_logement_2007-47">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The proportion of individual housing is stronger than in the rest of the country (61.5% versus 56.8%). One can see both a regional tendency (73.9% of individual housing for Nord-Pas-de-Calais)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEE_logement_2007_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE_logement_2007-47">[22]</a></sup> and as a consequence of the presence in Cambrai by the headquarters of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Groupe_Maison_Familiale&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Groupe Maison Familiale (page does not exist)">Maison Familiale</a> group, a national developer of detached houses which was particularly active in the years 1960 to 1980. Due to the relatively small size of the city and the high proportion of detached houses, Cambrai has few "<a href="/wiki/Housing_estate" title="Housing estate">estates</a>" where any social problems could be concentrated.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Primary_residence" title="Primary residence">Primary residences</a> dominate with 90.6%, versus 83% for the rest of the country, and one can especially note the very low proportion of <a href="/wiki/Holiday_cottage" title="Holiday cottage">secondary residences</a> in Cambrai: 0.3% compared with 9.2% for the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEE_r.C3.A9sidences_2007_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE_r.C3.A9sidences_2007-48">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG/220px-Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG/330px-Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG/440px-Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lotissement_Martin_Martine_ann%C3%A9es_1970.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A street of houses in the subdivision "Martin Martine" constructed by the <i>Maison Familiale</i> group, characteristic habitat of the years 1960-1970</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG/220px-Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG/330px-Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG/440px-Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_vieille_rue.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former habitat in the old Cambrai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The proportion of owners, at 46.4%, is lower than in the rest of the country (54.7%) or the region (55.1%). The tenants are much more numerous, 50.5% in Cambrai, against little more than 40% in the region and in France. Among rental housing, the proportion of <a href="/wiki/HLM" title="HLM">HLM</a> housing, at 19.2%, follows the regional trend of 20.4%, which is significantly higher than the national average of 16%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEE_r.C3.A9sidences_2007_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE_r.C3.A9sidences_2007-48">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[note 3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The age of the accommodation in Cambrai is distinguished from both regional and national averages. Housing is older, on average, in Cambrai than in the region or the country. The proportion of (pre-1949) "old" housing, is close to the regional average (40.6% at Cambrai against 39.9% for the region) but significantly higher than the French average of 32.9%. Meanwhile, dwellings built between 1949 and 1974 account for 42.9% of the total in Cambrai, significantly above the 31.5% of the region and 33% of the country. This proportion can probably be explained by the necessary reconstruction which followed the destruction of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, as well as programmes of Maison Familiale group homes, mentioned earlier, in the 1960s and 1970s. More recent housing is relatively less in the city than in the rest of France or even in the region: 11.8% of accommodation in Cambrai was built between 1975 and 1989, compared with 21.7% in the region and 23.7% in France; 4.6% have been built since 1990, compared with 6.8% in the Nord department and 10.4% in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEE_logement_2007_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE_logement_2007-47">[22]</a></sup> This is probably a consequence of the less dynamic economy and population of the city in recent years.</p>
<p>Finally, the accommodation is slightly better equipped than in the rest of the region in Cambrai, but rather less well than the French average:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEE_logement_2007_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE_logement_2007-47">[22]</a></sup> 3.8% have no bath or shower (2.3% in France, 4.7% in the region), 86.6% have central heating (78.2% in the region, 84.1% in France), and 4.3% have two bathrooms (4.4% in the region, 10% in France).</p>
<p>The agglomeration community seeks to improve the quality of the accommodation by various means: Encourage rehabilitation of vacant properties, expand available accommodation which is suitable for elderly or handicapped people, increase the supply of rentals and promote the construction of more energy efficient housing. The creation of 960 new social houses was provided over six years, from 2008 to 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAChabitat_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-CAChabitat-50">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Urban_social_cohesion_contract&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Urban social cohesion contract (page does not exist)">Urban social cohesion contract</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contrat_urbain_de_coh%C3%A9sion_sociale" title="fr:Contrat urbain de cohésion sociale">fr</a>)</span> signed in 2007 with the city and the urban community was the first of the Nord department. Five quarters, not classified as "sensitive urban areas", are concerned: The old centre where old habitat remains, the <i>l'Amérique</i> and <i>La Forêt</i> estates, consisting primarily of multi-family housing, and the <i>d'Esnes</i> and <i>de Guise</i> estates dominated by single-family housing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAChabitat_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-CAChabitat-50">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_projects">Development projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Development projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG/220px-Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG/330px-Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG/440px-Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canal_docks_cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The entrance from the Scheldt canal, the canal which serves the old docks and warehouses of Cambrai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, the projects of the municipality include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[25]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The "docks and warehouses," Brownfield site of 5 hectares (12 acres) at the edge of the Saint-Quentin canal, the assignment of which has not yet been determined but which should essentially be devoted to recreation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li>The rehabilitation of the centre of the Martin-Martine quarter, and in particular the transformation of the green corridor which was originally reserved for an "urban expressway", never realised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>The layout of the <i>Place du 9-Octobre</i> around the Church of Saint-Géry [Saint Gaugericus]</li>
<li>The redevelopment of the station quarter in the "exchange hub": A study on the development of the multimodal trade hub of Cambrai was launched in 2007 by the agglomeration community of Cambrai in partnership with the city, the Northern Department and the region, with purpose the station District redevelopment and improvement of <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_passenger_transport" title="Intermodal passenger transport">intermodality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>The relocation of the library to new premises.</li>
<li>The "modernisation" of the public garden.</li>
</ul>
<p>On the other hand, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plan_local_d%27urbanisme&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plan local d'urbanisme (page does not exist)">local urbanism plan</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plan_local_d%27urbanisme" title="fr:Plan local d'urbanisme">fr</a>)</span> revolves around eight themes: "Cambrai, an urban centre in the countryside", "Preserve and enhance the natural, rural and agricultural space", "Reclaim and restructure", "Render Cambrai fully in its <i>urbanity</i>", "Build upon the city of history", "Save and protect the environment, improve the quality of the living environment", "Ensuring economic and sustainable development", and also "Mastering travel or promoting changes in modes of transport".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The location is attested as <i>Camaracum</i> in the 4th century in the <a href="/wiki/Tabula_Peutingeriana" title="Tabula Peutingeriana">Peutinger Table</a> and <i>Cameracum</i> (no date). It recognises the Gallo-Roman suffix of Celtic origin <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Suffix_of_-acum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Suffix of -acum (page does not exist)"><i>-acum</i></a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffixe_-acum" title="fr:Suffixe -acum">fr</a>)</span> "place of", "property of", preceded by an element not identified with certainty. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Dauzat" title="Albert Dauzat">Albert Dauzat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rostaing" title="Charles Rostaing">Charles Rostaing</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[30]</a></sup> offered the Gallo-Roman type name of a person called Camarus.</p>
<p>This is also found in the anthroponym of <a href="/wiki/Chambray" title="Chambray">Chambray</a> (Eure) (<i>Cambracus</i> 1011, <i>Cameragus</i> to 1025). Variants <i>Cambarius</i> and <i>Camarius</i> would also explain <a href="/wiki/Cambayrac" title="Cambayrac">Cambayrac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chambry,_Aisne" title="Chambry, Aisne">Chambry</a> in Aine and <a href="/wiki/Chambry,_Seine-et-Marne" title="Chambry, Seine-et-Marne">the same</a> in Seine-et-Marne, <a href="/wiki/Chamery" title="Chamery">Chamery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A9mery" title="Chémery">Chémery</a>, etc. François de Beaurepaire<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[31]</a></sup> notes that it may also be a pre-Latin <i>camar</i> or <i>cambar</i> theme. However, Xavier Delamarre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[32]</a></sup> cited the personal name <i>Cambarius</i>, which he considers as based on the Gallic word <i>cambo-</i> "curve" (cf. old Irish <i>camb</i>, <i>camm</i> "curved", "bent" or "twisted"). <i>Camarus</i> would be a variant of this Gallic nickname meaning "that which is curved".</p>
<p>The Cambrai shape is Normanno-Picard with a hard "C", characteristic of the north of the <a href="/wiki/Joret_line" title="Joret line">Joret line</a> and therefore corresponds to the form of <a href="/wiki/Francien_language" title="Francien language">Francien</a> type Chambray. In addition, the name of the town was written <i>Cambray</i> until the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.</p>
<p>It is known under the name of <i>Kamerijk</i> in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[33]</a></sup> and formerly <i>Kamerich</i> in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
