</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="270" data-file-width="483" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg/220px-Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg/330px-Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg/440px-Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peutinger_Casaromago.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An extract from the Peutinger table showing Camaraco (Cambrai) northeast of Sammarobriva (present-day <a href="/wiki/Amiens" title="Amiens">Amiens</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Little is known with certainty of the beginnings of Cambrai. <i>Camaracum</i> or <i>Camaraco</i>, as it was known to the Romans, is mentioned for the first time on the <a href="/wiki/Tabula_Peutingeriana" title="Tabula Peutingeriana">Peutinger table</a> in the middle of the 4th century. It became the main town of the Roman province of the <a href="/wiki/Nervii" title="Nervii">Nervii</a>, whose first Roman capital had been at <i>Bagacum</i>, present-day <a href="/wiki/Bavay" title="Bavay">Bavay</a>.</p>
<p>In the middle of the 4th-century <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> raids from the north threatened Bavay and led the Romans to build forts along the Cologne to Bavay to Cambrai road, and thence to Boulogne. Cambrai thus occupied an important strategic position. In the early 5th century the town had become the administrative centre of the Nervii in replacement of Bavay which was probably too exposed to the Franks' raids and perhaps too damaged.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> arrived in the region at about the same time. A bishop of the Nervii by the name of <i>Superior</i> is mentioned in the middle of the 4th century, but nothing else is known about him.</p>
<p>In 430 the <a href="/wiki/Salian_Franks" title="Salian Franks">Salian Franks</a> under the command of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clodio" title="Clodio">Clodio</a> the Long-Haired took the town. In the 509 AD <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">Clovis</a> undertook to unify the Frankish kingdoms<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[b 10]</a></sup> by getting rid of his relatives. One of them was Ragnachar, who ruled over a small kingdom from Cambrai.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambrai began to grow from a rural market into a real city during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merovingian" title="Merovingian">Merovingian</a> times, a long period of peace when the bishoprics of Arras and Cambrai were first unified (probably owing to the small number of clerics left at the time) and were later transferred to Cambrai, an administrative centre for the region. Successive bishops, including <a href="/wiki/Gaugericus" title="Gaugericus">Gaugericus</a> (in French Géry), founded abbeys and churches to host relics, which contributed powerfully to giving Cambrai both the appearance and functions of a city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[b 11]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="660" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png/220px-Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png/330px-Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png/440px-Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trait%C3%A9_de_Verdun_843.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Following the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a>, Cambrai found itself as a "median" border city of the kingdom of Lothair I with the western lands of Charles the Bald</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a> in 843 split <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>'s empire into three parts, the county of Cambrai fell into <a href="/wiki/Lothair_I" title="Lothair I">Lothaire</a>'s kingdom. However, upon the death of <a href="/wiki/Lothair_II" title="Lothair II">Lothair II</a>, who had no heir, king <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bald" title="Charles the Bald">Charles the Bald</a> tried to gain control of his kingdom by having himself sacred at <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>. Cambrai thus reverted, but only briefly, to the <a href="/wiki/West_Francia" title="West Francia">Western Frankish Realm</a>. In 870 the town was destroyed by the Normans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 925 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_Germany" title="Henry I of Germany">Henry the Fowler</a> had regained control of Lothair's former domains. Cambrai henceforth belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, in an uncomfortable position on the border with France, until it was annexed by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> eight centuries later <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Cambrai_(1677)" title="Siege of Cambrai (1677)">after being captured</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a> in 1677.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beffoi_de_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The belfry of Cambrai, the old bell tower of the Church of Saint Martin, symbol of communal freedoms</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Middle Ages the region around Cambrai, called Cambrésis, was a county. Rivalries between the count, who ruled the city and county, and the bishop, ceased when in 948 <a href="/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto I</a> granted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Cambrai" title="Archdiocese of Cambrai">bishop</a> with temporal powers over the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[b 12]</a></sup> In 1007, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Henry_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry II, Holy Roman Emperor">Henry II</a> extended the bishop's temporal power to the territory surrounding Cambrai. The bishops then had both spiritual and temporal powers. This made Cambrai and Cambrésis a church principality, much like <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a>, an independent state which was part of the Holy Roman Empire. The spiritual power of the bishop was exercised over a vast diocese, which stretched on the right bank of the Scheldt to <a href="/wiki/Mons" title="Mons">Mons</a>, Brussels and Antwerp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[35]</a></sup> In 953, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Magyars</a> besieged Cambrai, which resisted all their attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 958 one of the first <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">communal</a> uprisings in Europe occurred in Cambrai. The inhabitants rebelled against Bishop Bérenger's power and abuses. The rebellion was severely repressed, but the discontent flared up again in the 10th and 11th centuries. Between 1077 and 1215, the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">burghers</a> had a charter franchise on at least four occasions. Each time, these were eventually withdrawn by the combined efforts of the bishops and emperors. In 1227, following another period of unrest, the burghers of Cambrai finally had to give up their charters and accept the bishop's authority. However, the <i>Loi Godefroid</i> promulgated by the bishop, in fact or in law, left the people a number of freedoms won in the management of communal affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambrai is also known for its Irish <a href="/wiki/Cambrai_Homily" title="Cambrai Homily">homily</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_activity">Economic activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economic activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_(Atlas_van_Loon).jpg"><img alt="Plan of Cambrai drawn in  1649" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4405" data-file-width="5500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg/220px-Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg/330px-Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg/440px-Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_%28Atlas_van_Loon%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_-_Cameracvm_vulgo_Cambray_-_Kamerijk_(Atlas_van_Loon).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Plan of Cambrai drawn in 1649, depicting the outline of the 11th century walls</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Middle Ages the city grew richer and larger thanks to its weaving industry which produced woollen cloth, linen and <a href="/wiki/Cambric" title="Cambric">cambric</a>. Cambrai, and in particular the drapery, experienced an economic decline from the 15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[b 13]</a></sup> Cambrai then belonged to a commercial <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">hansa</a> of seventeen low country cities whose aim was to develop trade with the fairs in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Champagne,_France" title="Champagne, France">Champagne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. By the 11th century the city walls had reached the circumference they would keep until the 19th century.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_history">Music history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Music history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DufayBinchois.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="373" data-file-width="418" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/DufayBinchois.jpg/200px-DufayBinchois.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/DufayBinchois.jpg/300px-DufayBinchois.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/DufayBinchois.jpg/400px-DufayBinchois.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DufayBinchois.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dufay (left) in conversation with <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Binchois" title="Gilles Binchois">Gilles Binchois</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai has a distinguished musical history, particularly in the 15th century. The <a href="/wiki/Old_Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Old Cambrai Cathedral">cathedral</a> there, a musical center until the 17th century, had one of the most active musical establishments in the Low Countries; many composers of the <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_School" title="Burgundian School">Burgundian School</a> either grew up and learned their craft there, or returned to teach. In 1428 Philippe de Luxembourg claimed that the cathedral was the finest in all of Christianity, for the fineness of its singing, its light, and the sweetness of its bells. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guillaume_Dufay" title="Guillaume Dufay">Guillaume Dufay</a>, the most famous European musician of the 15th century, studied at the cathedral from 1409 to 1412, and returned in 1439 after spending many years in Italy. Cambrai cathedral had other famous composers in the later 15th century: <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Tinctoris" title="Johannes Tinctoris">Johannes Tinctoris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Ockeghem" title="Johannes Ockeghem">Ockeghem</a> went to Cambrai to study with Dufay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[b 14]</a></sup> Other composers included <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Grenon" title="Nicolas Grenon">Nicolas Grenon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Agricola" title="Alexander Agricola">Alexander Agricola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Obrecht" title="Jacob Obrecht">Jacob Obrecht</a>. In the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Philippe_de_Monte" title="Philippe de Monte">Philippe de Monte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Lupi" title="Johannes Lupi">Johannes Lupi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jacobus_de_Kerle" title="Jacobus de Kerle">Jacobus de Kerle</a> all worked there.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hundred_Years.27_War">Hundred Years' War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Hundred Years' War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Even though the bishop tried to preserve the independence of his small state of Cambrésis, the task was not easy, wedged as the county was between its more powerful neighbours the counts of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a>, of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Hainaut" title="County of Hainaut">Hainaut</a> and the kings of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, especially during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a>. In 1339, in the early stages of the war, the English king <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward III</a> laid siege to the city but eventually had to withdraw. By the 14th century the county was surrounded on all parts by <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">Burgundy</a>'s possessions and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_of_Burgundy,_Bishop_of_Cambrai" title="John of Burgundy, Bishop of Cambrai">John of Burgundy</a>, an illegitimate son of <a href="/wiki/John_the_Fearless" title="John the Fearless">John the Fearless</a>, was made bishop. However what looked like an impending annexation of Cambrésis to the states of Burgundy was made impossible by the sudden death of <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bold" title="Charles the Bold">Charles the Bold</a> in 1477. <a href="/wiki/Louis_XI_of_France" title="Louis XI of France">Louis XI</a> immediately seized the opportunity to take control of Cambrai, but left the city a year later.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_legend_of_Martin_and_Martine">The legend of Martin and Martine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: The legend of Martin and Martine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Martin and Martine are two legendary characters who have come to represent the city which they are said to have saved. There are different versions of the story. The most commonly accepted version runs as follows: around the year 1370, at the time of Bishop Robert, Count of Geneva, Martin, a blacksmith of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorish" title="Moorish">Moorish</a> descent established in Cambrai, was among the burghers who left the city to fight the lord of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thun-L%C3%A9v%C3%AAque&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thun-Lévêque (page does not exist)">Thun-Lévêque</a>, who was then reputed to ransom the population around the city and generally to afflict the region. Martin, armed only with his heavy iron hammer, soon came face to face with the enemy. He dealt such a heavy blow on his opponent's head that, although the helmet of the lord did not break, because it was made of good steel, it was driven down to his eyes. Dazed and blinded, the lord of Thun quickly surrendered. Today the automatons of Martin and Martine, standing at the top of the town hall, strike the hours with a hammer as a reminder of that mighty blow.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Modern_era">Early Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Early Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1360" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maison_des_Canonniers_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "gunners' house" in Cambrai is an example of 17th-century Flemish architecture</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg"><img alt="Plan of Cambrai in 1710" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1884" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg/220px-Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg/330px-Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg/440px-Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Cambrai_1710.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Plan of Cambrai in 1710</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the economic centre of northern Europe moved away from <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a>, the area became poorer, with an associated period of cultural decline. However the city's neutrality and its position between the possessions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> made it the venue of several international negotiations, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_of_Cambrai" title="League of Cambrai">League of Cambrai</a>, an alliance engineered in 1508 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Pope Julius II</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a>, concluding in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Cambrai" title="Treaty of Cambrai">Treaty of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trait%C3%A9_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Traité de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>. The alliance collapsed in 1510 when the Pope allied with Venice against his former ally <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. The conflict is also referred to as the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_League_of_Cambrai" title="War of the League of Cambrai">War of the League of Cambrai</a> and lasted from 1508 to 1516. Cambrai was also the site of negotiations in 1529, concluding in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paix_des_Dames" title="Paix des Dames">Paix des Dames</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paix_des_Dames" title="fr:Paix des Dames">fr</a>)</span>, which led to France's withdrawal from the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_League_of_Cognac" title="War of the League of Cognac">War of the League of Cognac</a>.</p>
<p>In 1543 Cambrai was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, and annexed to his already vast possessions. He had the medieval monastery of Saint-Sépulchre demolished and a citadel built in its place.</p>
<p>In 1623, the community of nuns of the <a href="/wiki/English_Benedictine_Congregation" title="English Benedictine Congregation">English Benedictine Congregation</a> was founded at Cambrai. Expelled in 1793 as a result of the French Revolution, its successor community has since 1838 been established at <a href="/wiki/Stanbrook_Abbey" title="Stanbrook Abbey">Stanbrook Abbey</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Malvern,_Worcestershire" title="Malvern, Worcestershire">Malvern</a>.</p>
<p>In 1630, <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Richelieu" title="Cardinal Richelieu">Richelieu</a>, wishing to counter the power of the Emperor and Spain, renewed the alliance of France with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a>. The main effort of France had to focus on the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a>, and a sharing plan was established with the Dutch, with France to receive the Hainaut, Cambrésis, Artois, a large part of Flanders and Luxembourg and the County of Namur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War#French_intervention_and_continued_Swedish_participation_.281635.E2.80.931648.29" title="Thirty Years' War">War</a> was declared against Spain in 1635: It was followed by a <a href="/wiki/Franco-Spanish_War_(1635%E2%80%9359)" title="Franco-Spanish War (1635–59)">long series of wars</a> which, compounded by subsistence and epidemics, caused crises which would bruise the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Cambrésis">Cambrésis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trenard145_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trenard145-70">[b 15]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Mazarin" title="Cardinal Mazarin">Mazarin</a> tried unsuccessfully, in 1649, to seize the city which was being besieged by <a href="/wiki/Henri,_Count_of_Harcourt" title="Henri, Count of Harcourt">Henri de Lorraine-Harcourt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Henri_de_la_Tour_d%27Auvergne,_Vicomte_de_Turenne" title="Henri de la Tour d'Auvergne, Vicomte de Turenne">Vicomte de Turenne</a>. A Spanish regiment, which came from <a href="/wiki/Bouchain" title="Bouchain">Bouchain</a> succeeded in entering the city and the siege was lifted. In 1657, the Vicomte de Turenne captured Cambrai. Again 4,000 horsemen under the command of <a href="/wiki/Louis,_Grand_Cond%C3%A9" title="Louis, Grand Condé">Condé</a>, in the service of the Spain, manage to penetrate, and Turenne abandoned the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[b 16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1666, in the greatest secrecy, <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV</a> prepared new conquests by making plans of the Spanish fortifications, and then began the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Devolution" title="War of Devolution">War of Devolution</a>. If the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1668)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1668)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a> from 1668 allowed the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a> to obtain a large number of strongholds, Cambrai was not a part, nor <a href="/wiki/Bouchain" title="Bouchain">Bouchain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valenciennes" title="Valenciennes">Valenciennes</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9-sur-l%27Escaut" title="Condé-sur-l'Escaut">Condé-sur-l'Escaut</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_annexation_by_France">The annexation by France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: The annexation by France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1672, <a href="/wiki/Franco-Dutch_War" title="Franco-Dutch War">hostilities</a> resumed against the Protestant Republic of the Netherlands and continued in the following years. In 1676, <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV</a>, in an effort to "safeguard the tranquility of his borders for ever" ("<i>assurer à jamais le repos de ses frontières</i>"), focused most of his efforts against Spain and occupied <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9-sur-l%27Escaut" title="Condé-sur-l'Escaut">Condé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bouchain" title="Bouchain">Bouchain</a>. On 17 March 1677, the French troops <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Valenciennes_(1676%E2%80%9377)" title="Siege of Valenciennes (1676–77)">stormed Valenciennes</a> and moved toward Cambrai, the strongest place of the Netherlands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[b 17]</a></sup> which was reached on 20 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[39]</a></sup> On 22 March, Louis XIV was in the city in person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[b 18]</a></sup> On 2 April, the French invested in a part of the place. By 5 April, the city surrendered, given the same benefits as Lille in 1667,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[b 19]</a></sup> but the Spanish garrison took refuge in the <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">citadel</a> and the siege continued until 17 April. After <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Cambrai_(1677)" title="Siege of Cambrai (1677)">29 days of siege</a> the king made his entry into the city, on 19 April, Easter Monday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[b 20]</a></sup> Louis XIV named the Marquis de Cesen as governor, and appointed 14 new <a href="/wiki/Alderman" title="Alderman">aldermen</a> while keeping the same <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pr%C3%A9v%C3%B4t_(Ancien_R%C3%A9gime)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prévôt (Ancien Régime) (page does not exist)">provost</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pr%C3%A9v%C3%B4t_(Ancien_R%C3%A9gime)" title="fr:Prévôt (Ancien Régime)">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<p>By the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nijmegen" title="Treaty of Nijmegen">Treaty of Nijmegen</a> of 1678, Spain had relinquished Cambrai, which has remained as a part of France, to this day.</p>
<p>French influence would transform the architecture and urbanism of the city. The gables of the houses on the street were blocked and the city was embellished with mansions. The fortifications were reinforced with advanced works. The first archbishop appointed by the king of France was <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_F%C3%A9nelon" title="François Fénelon">François Fénelon</a>. He came to be known as the "Swan of Cambrai" ("<i>le cygne de Cambrai</i>"), in opposition to his friend and rival <a href="/wiki/Jacques-B%C3%A9nigne_Bossuet" title="Jacques-Bénigne Bossuet">Bossuet</a>, the "eagle of Meaux" ("<i>l'aigle de Meaux</i>"), and he wrote his <i>Maxims of the Saints</i> while residing in the city. He had a relentless zeal to enlighten the faithful and to convert the unfaithful.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_French_Revolution">The French Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: The French Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city suffered from the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">Revolution</a>: <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Le_Bon" title="Joseph Le Bon">Joseph Le Bon</a>, sent by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comit%C3%A9_de_salut_public" title="Comité de salut public">Comité de salut public</a>, arrived in Cambrai in 1794. He was to set up an era of "terror", sending many to the <a href="/wiki/Guillotine" title="Guillotine">guillotine</a>, until he was tried and executed in 1795. Most of the religious buildings of the city were demolished in that period: in 1797, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Old Cambrai Cathedral">old cathedral</a>, which had been dubbed the "wonder of the low countries", was sold to a merchant on 6 June 1796 who left only the tower,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[d 2]</a></sup> after exploiting the cathedral as a stone quarry. The main tower was left standing until 1809, when it collapsed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[d 3]</a></sup> in a storm. However the cathedral's archives have been preserved (they are now at the Archives Départementales du Nord in <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>) and a <a href="/wiki/Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Cambrai Cathedral">new cathedral</a> was later provided.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1360" data-file-width="2048" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boulevard_Faidherbe_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Boulevard Faidherbe, drawn in 1898 on the site of the ramparts.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> of 1870 widely spared Cambrai. It also showed the futility of the fortifications which the city obtained permission to demolish, at its expense, in 1892.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[b 21]</a></sup> The outer boulevards were constructed and off to the location of the walls, between 1894 and the beginning of the 20th century. The appearance of the city was radically transformed, and the works stimulated the city's economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[b 22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1058" data-file-width="1640" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG/220px-LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG/330px-LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG/440px-LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LL_16_-_Cambrai_-_Vue_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_vers_la_Place_d%27Armes.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Place d'Armes</i>, on a market day before the First World War</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09,_Frankreich,_Cambrai,_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="556" data-file-width="800" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09%2C_Frankreich%2C_Cambrai%2C_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09%2C_Frankreich%2C_Cambrai%2C_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09%2C_Frankreich%2C_Cambrai%2C_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09%2C_Frankreich%2C_Cambrai%2C_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09%2C_Frankreich%2C_Cambrai%2C_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09%2C_Frankreich%2C_Cambrai%2C_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-029-09,_Frankreich,_Cambrai,_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Refugees at Cambrai in September 1918</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle" role="note">Main articles: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction_in_France_and_in_Belgium_after_World_War_I&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Reconstruction in France and in Belgium after World War I (page does not exist)">Reconstruction in France and in Belgium after World War I</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_en_France_et_en_Belgique_apr%C3%A8s_la_Premi%C3%A8re_Guerre_mondiale" title="fr:Reconstruction en France et en Belgique après la Première Guerre mondiale">fr</a>)</span>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction_after_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Reconstruction after World War II (page does not exist)">Reconstruction after World War II</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_apr%C3%A8s_la_Seconde_Guerre_mondiale" title="fr:Reconstruction après la Seconde Guerre mondiale">fr</a>)</span></div>
<p>In 1914, the German army occupied the city: This occupation, which lasted for four years, was marked by scenes of looting, requisitions and arrests of hostages. From 20 November to 17 December 1917, the vicinity of the town of Cambrai was the theatre of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1917)" title="Battle of Cambrai (1917)">Battle of Cambrai</a>, which saw the massive use of <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tanks</a> for the first time.</p>
<p>In 1918, the Germans burned the city centre before leaving, destroying the city hall and the municipal archives. In total, more than 1,500 buildings were totally destroyed, of the 3,500 which consisted of Cambrai. The centre was to be rebuilt, a task which was entrusted to the architect <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Leprince-Ringuet (page does not exist)">Pierre Leprince-Ringuet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet" title="fr:Pierre Leprince-Ringuet">fr</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[b 23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[b 24]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> also struck Cambrai. The city was bombed by the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> on 17 May 1940, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Battle of France</a>, before falling the next day at the same time as <a href="/wiki/Saint-Quentin,_Aisne" title="Saint-Quentin, Aisne">Saint-Quentin</a>. The remains of the <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Army_(France)" title="Ninth Army (France)">9th French Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henri_Giraud" title="Henri Giraud">General Giraud</a> were taken prisoner by the Germans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 27 April until 18 August 1944, 18 <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> air raids were directed against the railway tracks, killing 250 people and destroying 1,700 buildings,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[b 25]</a></sup> or more than 50% of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[42]</a></sup> The first American tanks entered the city on 2 September.</p>
<p>After the war, the priority again was reconstruction. A municipality of the "union of the left" was elected in 1945, led by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Raymond_Gernez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Raymond Gernez (page does not exist)">Raymond Gernez</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_Gernez" title="fr:Raymond Gernez">fr</a>)</span> who would remain at the head of the city until 1981, promoting moderate Socialism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[b 26]</a></sup> As early as 1947, the city submitted to a development project of the Ministry of Reconstruction. The municipality gave priority to the construction of houses: The <i>Maison du Cambrésis</i> [House of le Cambrésis], later <i>Maison Familiale</i> group, an <a href="/wiki/HLM" title="HLM">HLM</a> cooperative society, contributed substantially to the reconstruction of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[b 27]</a></sup> The population of the city progressed, while the arrondissement tended to be depopulated. At the same time, the city lost industrial jobs and moved towards the tertiary sector, but it was public administrations which provided the bulk of jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[b 28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_administration">Politics and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Politics and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_trends_and_results">Political trends and results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Political trends and results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Municipal_elections_in_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Municipal elections in Cambrai (page does not exist)">Municipal elections in Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89lections_municipales_%C3%A0_Cambrai" title="fr:Élections municipales à Cambrai">fr</a>)</span></div>
<p>Overall, voting in Cambrai is little different from the national vote, but the abstention rate is often higher: For example, it was 34.86% in the 2005 referendum (against 30.63%); 22.07% in the first round of the 2007 presidential election (compared with 16.23%) and 38.13% in the first round of the legislative elections of 2002 (compared to 35.58%).</p>
<p>Cambresiens voters seem also more cautious with regard to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the French in general: The <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> on the ratification of the Treaty on European Union of 1992 was rejected by 53.35%, while at the national level it was approved by a narrow majority of 51.04%. In 2005, the draft law on the ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe</a> was rejected more widely in Cambrai (59.8% of voted "No") than at the national level (54.67%).</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/French_presidential_election,_2007" title="French presidential election, 2007">presidential election of 2007</a> the results of the second round were very close to national figures: 54.07% for <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> and 45.93% for <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9gol%C3%A8ne_Royal" title="Ségolène Royal">Ségolène Royal</a>, against respectively 53.06% and 46.94% at the national level. In the first round <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen" title="Jean-Marie Le Pen">Jean-Marie Le Pen</a> achieved a slightly better result at Cambrai (13.28%) than France (10.44%), while <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Bayrou" title="François Bayrou">François Bayrou</a> was in a reversed situation (16.77% against 18.57%). <a href="/wiki/Arlette_Laguiller" title="Arlette Laguiller">Arlette Laguiller</a> (2.02%) and <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Besancenot" title="Olivier Besancenot">Olivier Besancenot</a> (4.77%) were the only other candidates to exceed 1.5%. In the second round of the <a href="/wiki/French_presidential_election,_2002" title="French presidential election, 2002">presidential election of 2002</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Chirac" title="Jacques Chirac">Jacques Chirac</a> arrived largely in the lead in Cambrai as in the rest of the country but Jean-Marie Le Pen's result was higher (21.11% against 17.79%).</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/French_legislative_election,_2007" title="French legislative election, 2007">legislative elections of 2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Xavier_Villain" title="François-Xavier Villain">François-Xavier Villain</a>, the candidate related to the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_a_Popular_Movement" title="Union for a Popular Movement">UMP</a> and who was also the incumbent Mayor of Cambrai, achieved 57.42% in the first round (48.03% in the constituency). All the other candidates were below the national percentage of their party. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(France)" title="Socialist Party (France)">Socialist Party</a> achieved 22.91% against 24.73%, the <a href="/wiki/French_Communist_Party" title="French Communist Party">Communist Party</a> at 3.10% compared to 4.29% and the UDF at 6.21% against 7.61%. The decline of the <a href="/wiki/National_Front_(France)" title="National Front (France)">National Front</a> was also more marked in Cambrai (4.14%) than elsewhere (4.24%). One finds a situation close to the <a href="/wiki/French_legislative_election,_2002" title="French legislative election, 2002">2002 elections</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the first round of the <a href="/wiki/French_presidential_election,_2012" title="French presidential election, 2012">presidential election of 2012</a>, the four candidates in the lead in Cambrai were <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Union_for_a_Popular_Movement" title="Union for a Popular Movement">UMP</a>, 28.29%), <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> (<a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(France)" title="Socialist Party (France)">PS</a>, 27.56%), <a href="/wiki/Marine_Le_Pen" title="Marine Le Pen">Marine Le Pen</a> (<a href="/wiki/National_Front_(France)" title="National Front (France)">FN</a>, 20.81%) and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_M%C3%A9lenchon" title="Jean-Luc Mélenchon">Jean-Luc Mélenchon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Left_Front_(France)" title="Left Front (France)">Left Front</a>, 10.14%) with a turnout of 72.61%. In the second round, François Hollande was in the lead with 50.75% of the vote, with a participation rate of 73.09%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_government">Municipal government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Municipal government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="295" data-file-width="450" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg/220px-Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg/330px-Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg/440px-Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai-H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The city hall, inaugurated in 1932</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chef-lieu" title="Chef-lieu">chef-lieu</a> of one of the six <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement_of_Cambrai" title="Arrondissement of Cambrai">arrondissements</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Nord_(French_department)" title="Nord (French department)">Nord department</a>.</p>
<p>Cambrai is divided into two <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_France" title="Cantons of France">cantons</a>: The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canton_of_Cambrai-East&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canton of Cambrai-East (page does not exist)">Canton of Cambrai-East</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canton_de_Cambrai-Est" title="fr:Canton de Cambrai-Est">fr</a>)</span> (22,942 inhabitants in 1999) and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canton_of_Cambrai-West&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canton of Cambrai-West (page does not exist)">Canton of Cambrai-West</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canton_de_Cambrai-Ouest" title="fr:Canton de Cambrai-Ouest">fr</a>)</span> (39,821 inhabitants in 1999).</p>
<p>Since 22 December 1992, Cambrai is the seat of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Agglomeration_Community_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Agglomeration Community of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Agglomeration Community of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communaut%C3%A9_d%27agglom%C3%A9ration_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Communauté d'agglomération de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span> which includes 33 communes and approximately 68,000 inhabitants. The city also adheres to the following intercommunal structures:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Intercommunal Association of Sanitation of the Cambrai Agglomeration (SIAC).</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Single-purpose_intercommunal_syndicate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Single-purpose intercommunal syndicate (page does not exist)">SIVU</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syndicat_intercommunal_%C3%A0_vocation_unique" title="fr:Syndicat intercommunal à vocation unique">fr</a>)</span> <i>"Scènes mitoyennes"</i> ["Adjoining Stages"], created in August 2000, brings together the communes of Cambrai, <a href="/wiki/Caudry" title="Caudry">Caudry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Escaud%C5%93uvres" title="Escaudœuvres">Escaudœuvres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neuville-Saint-R%C3%A9my" title="Neuville-Saint-Rémy">Neuville-Saint-Rémy</a> with which it harmonises cultural policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>SIVU <i>"Murs mitoyens"</i> ["Adjoining Walls"], operational since 1 January 2006 and headquartered in Caudry, its mission is to educate the various planning authorities for the two cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Intercommunity Association of the energy of the Cambrésis (SIDEC), which is headquartered at Neuville-Saint-Rémy, brings together the 111 communes in the arrondissement. It concedes the management of the public service energy distribution to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9_R%C3%A9seau_Distribution_France" title="Électricité Réseau Distribution France">ERDF</a> and manages the work of strengthening and concealment of networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Scheme_of_territorial_coherence&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Scheme of territorial coherence (page does not exist)">Scheme of territorial coherence</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sch%C3%A9ma_de_coh%C3%A9rence_territoriale" title="fr:Schéma de cohérence territoriale">fr</a>)</span> (SCoT) of le Cambrésis (via the agglomeration community of Cambrai).</li>
<li>The Joint Association for the Enhancement of the Upper Scheldt (via the agglomeration community of Cambrai).</li>
</ul>
<p>Cambrai was merged with the commune of <a href="/wiki/Morenchies" title="Morenchies">Morenchies</a> in 1971.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_mayors">List of mayors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: List of mayors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_mayors_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of mayors of Cambrai (page does not exist)">List of mayors of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liste_des_maires_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Liste des maires de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span></div>
<p>Since 1945, Cambrai has had three mayors. The city, after having constantly re-elected a <a href="/wiki/French_Section_of_the_Workers%27_International" title="French Section of the Workers' International">Socialist</a> mayor from the Liberation until 1977 in the person of Raymond Gernez, has since been administered by mayors from RPR or the related UMP: Jacques Legendre until 1992, then François-Xavier Villain. The latter was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Nord%27s_18th_constituency" title="Nord's 18th constituency">18th constituency in Nord</a> on 16 June 2002 and re-elected in 2007 and 2012.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_and_administrative_authorities">Judicial and administrative authorities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Judicial and administrative authorities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambrai was for a short time the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Parlement" title="Parlement">Parlement</a>, from 1709 until its transfer to <a href="/wiki/Douai" title="Douai">Douai</a> in 1713.</p>
<p>The city is now within the jurisdiction of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Court_of_Appeal_of_Douai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Court of Appeal of Douai (page does not exist)">Court of Appeal of Douai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cour_d%27appel_de_Douai" title="fr:Cour d'appel de Douai">fr</a>)</span>. It is the seat of a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tribunal_de_grande_instance_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tribunal de grande instance (France) (page does not exist)">high court</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribunal_de_grande_instance_(France)" title="fr:Tribunal de grande instance (France)">fr</a>)</span> whose jurisdiction coincides with the boundaries of the <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement" title="Arrondissement">arrondissement</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tribunal_d%27instance" title="Tribunal d'instance">Tribunal d'instance</a> and an <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Conseil_de_prud%27hommes_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Conseil de prud'hommes (France) (page does not exist)">industrial tribunal</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conseil_de_prud%27hommes_(France)" title="fr:Conseil de prud'hommes (France)">fr</a>)</span>, installed in the restored <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Château de Selles (page does not exist)">Château de Selles</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles" title="fr:Château de Selles">fr</a>)</span>. With the reform of the judicial map launched in 2007 the city has lost its <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tribunal_de_commerce_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tribunal de commerce (France) (page does not exist)">commercial court</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribunal_de_commerce_(France)" title="fr:Tribunal de commerce (France)">fr</a>)</span> and is linked to that of Douai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_policy">Environmental policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Environmental policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beginning 2010, the city's environmental policy seems difficult to read: There is a Directorate for the Environment at the mayor's office but the site fails to deliver any information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The environmental policy is one of the competences of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_the_agglomeration_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Community of the agglomeration of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Community of the agglomeration of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communaut%C3%A9_d%27agglom%C3%A9ration_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Communauté d'agglomération de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_France" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in France">List of twin towns and sister cities in France</a></div>
<p>Cambrai is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JUMEL_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-JUMEL-98">[51]</a></sup> with:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kamp-Lintfort" title="Kamp-Lintfort">Kamp-Lintfort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, since 1970</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teauguay" title="Châteauguay">Châteauguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, since 1980</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Houma,_Louisiana" title="Houma, Louisiana">Houma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, since 1986</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravesend,_Kent" title="Gravesend, Kent">Gravesend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Archant_twinning_3_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Archant_twinning_3-99">[52]</a></sup> since 1989</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary"><img alt="Hungary" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Esztergom" title="Esztergom">Esztergom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, since 1991</li>
</ul>
<p>An agreement of pre-twinning with the city of <a href="/wiki/Cieszyn" title="Cieszyn">Cieszyn</a> in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> was signed Friday, 15 July 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[53]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_society">Population and society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Population and society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, the commune had 32,847 inhabitants. The evolution of the number of inhabitants is known through the population censuses carried out in the town since 1793. From the 21st century, the communes with more than 10,000 inhabitants have a census take place every year as a result of a sample survey, unlike the other communes which have a real census every five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[note 4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[note 5]</a></sup></p>

</tr>
</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Urban_unit" title="Urban unit">urban unit</a> of Cambrai had 47,138 inhabitants in 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[57]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">urban area</a> 65,986 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[58]</a></sup> In other less populated regions, Cambrai would be an important city, but in <a href="/wiki/Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="Nord-Pas-de-Calais">Nord-Pas-de-Calais</a>, densely populated and urbanised, the city and its suburbs come far behind <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a> (1,143,125 inhabitants), <a href="/wiki/Douai" title="Douai">Douai</a>-<a href="/wiki/Lens,_Pas-de-Calais" title="Lens, Pas-de-Calais">Lens</a> (552,682), <a href="/wiki/Valenciennes" title="Valenciennes">Valenciennes</a> (399,677), <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a> (265,974) and <a href="/wiki/Maubeuge" title="Maubeuge">Maubeuge</a> (125,000), and tied with <a href="/wiki/Armenti%C3%A8res" title="Armentières">Armentières</a> (58,706).</p>
<p>The population of Cambrai increased little over the centuries: Estimated at 10,000 souls in the 15th century, it is, according to a memorandum of intendant who described it as "very diminished", at 12,000 in 1698.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[b 29]</a></sup> At the end of the Revolution, in 1801, it was still only approximately 15,000 inhabitants.</p>
<p>It increased slowly but steadily throughout the 19th century with a net decline in the early 20th century: the birth rate, as everywhere else in France, declined. At the same time, infant mortality remained high (20.3% in 1900, 10.2% on the eve of the war),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[b 30]</a></sup> which explains the low natural growth.</p>
<p>The population growth resumed at a rapid pace between the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and the beginning of the 1970s (the <a href="/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses" title="Trente Glorieuses">Trente Glorieuses</a>), through <a href="/wiki/Rate_of_natural_increase" title="Rate of natural increase">natural increase</a> (<a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_baby_boom" title="Post–World War II baby boom">baby boomers</a> and sharp decline of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Rural_flight" title="Rural flight">rural exodus</a>, which slowly emptied the villages of Cambrésis of their population (partial) towards the town of Cambrai. This dynamism, however, showed however signs of stalling since 1968: in fact the progress of jobs (+27.5% from 1952 to 1975) did not follow that of the population (+44.2%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[b 31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The curve was brutally reversed by the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>. The city's population plummeted from the 1975 census, net migration which was largely positive in the 1960s became negative, while the natural balance, which remains positive, tends to shrink. Many traditional activities have disappeared (chocolate production, brewery, chicory, weaving, metallurgy, etc.), representing several thousand jobs.</p>

<p>The age structure of Cambrai at the census of 2007 was quite close to that of metropolitan France, and the Nord, with a greater deficit in the 0–14 years age group and to a lesser extent the age group of 30–44 years, a possible consequence of a negative migration balance.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_distribution">Population distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Population distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The population distribution of Cambrai (active population aged 15 or more in employment) by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Professions_and_socioprofessional_categories_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Professions and socioprofessional categories in France (page does not exist)">socio-professional category</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professions_et_cat%C3%A9gories_socioprofessionnelles_en_France" title="fr:Professions et catégories socioprofessionnelles en France">fr</a>)</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[62]</a></sup> showed an under-representation of managers and higher intellectual professionals (11.15%) with the French average (15.82%), in 2007, and vice versa slightly higher proportions of <a href="/wiki/Manual_labour" title="Manual labour">manual workers</a> (25.47% compared with 23.08%), of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Employee" title="Employee">employees</a> (31,37% against 28.40%) and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Profession_interm%C3%A9diaire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Profession intermédiaire (page does not exist)">intermediate professionals</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Profession_interm%C3%A9diaire" title="fr:Profession intermédiaire">fr</a>)</span> (26,41% 24.76%). The percentage of <a href="/wiki/Farmer" title="Farmer">farmers</a> is naturally low in Cambrai (0.42%).</p>
<p>The distribution of the population over the age of 15 years, and not enrolled in study,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[63]</a></sup> showed rates comparable to those of metropolitan France, in 2007, for level III and IV (Baccalauréat or Bac+2 years of study). However, it was behind the French average, and even the region, in relation to higher education (levels I and II).</p>
