<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambrai is the seat of a pool of training divided into three districts (Cambrai-North, Cambrai-South and Cambrai-Le Cateau) and dependent on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Direction_des_services_d%C3%A9partementaux_de_l%27%C3%89ducation_nationale&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Direction des services départementaux de l'Éducation nationale (page does not exist)">Education Authorities</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direction_des_services_d%C3%A9partementaux_de_l%27%C3%89ducation_nationale" title="fr:Direction des services départementaux de l'Éducation nationale">fr</a>)</span> of <a href="/wiki/Nord_(French_department)" title="Nord (French department)">Nord</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Lille" title="Academy of Lille">Academy of Lille</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city administers twelve <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_maternelle_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École maternelle in France (page does not exist)">nursery schools</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89cole_maternelle_en_France" title="fr:École maternelle en France">fr</a>)</span>, and eleven <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_%C3%A9l%C3%A9mentaire_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École élémentaire in France (page does not exist)">elementary schools</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89cole_%C3%A9l%C3%A9mentaire_en_France" title="fr:École élémentaire en France">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<p>The department manages four <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coll%C3%A8ge_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Collège in France (page does not exist)">colleges</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge_en_France" title="fr:Collège en France">fr</a>)</span>: Jules-Ferry, Fénelon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f.C3.A9nelon_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-f.C3.A9nelon-117">[65]</a></sup> Lamartine and Paul-Duez.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="Nord-Pas-de-Calais">Nord-Pas-de-Calais</a> region operates four <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lyc%C3%A9e_en_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lycée en France (page does not exist)">high schools</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_en_France" title="fr:Lycée en France">fr</a>)</span>: Fénelon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f.C3.A9nelon_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-f.C3.A9nelon-117">[65]</a></sup> Paul-Duez<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[66]</a></sup> and the vocational <a href="/wiki/Louise_de_Bettignies" title="Louise de Bettignies">Louise de Bettignies</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[67]</a></sup> and Louis-Blériot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[68]</a></sup> Cambrai also has a private institution, the ensemble of Saint-Luc, bringing together three former private schools merged in September 2009: Collège Jeanne d'Arc, Institution Notre Dame de Grace (college and high school of general and technological education) and the vocational high school La Sagresse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saintluc_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-saintluc-121">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_life">University life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: University life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambrai hosts two branches of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Valenciennes_and_Hainaut-Cambresis" title="University of Valenciennes and Hainaut-Cambresis">University of Valenciennes and Hainaut-Cambresis</a> (UVHC), and <a href="/wiki/Lille_2_University_of_Health_and_Law" title="Lille 2 University of Health and Law">Lille-2</a>.</p>
<p>UVHC antenna prepares eleven diplomas, which include of DUT, IUP, Master Pro, professional licenses (including "Cultural Actions and Promotion of Heritage" and "Trades of Archaeology") and licenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The branch of Lille-2 prepares to obtain a license "mention droit" or "mention economic and social administration", as well as three professional licenses: For management of small-medium businesses, for transportation of goods and for security professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally, Catholic teaching. The whole of Saint Luc de Cambrai<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saintluc_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-saintluc-121">[69]</a></sup> was a centre of higher education (Sup'Sagesse) from Bac+1 to Bac+5: BTS optician, BTS insurance, NRC, MUC, AG and AM, two professional licenses ("Operational Marketing Manager" and "Contingency Insurance and Management of Goods") and finally a Professional Master of "Entrepreneurial Strategy and Management", opened to the entrepreneurs.</p>
<p>With nearly 500 students in alternation, learning or school track, Sup'Sagesse<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saintluc_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-saintluc-121">[69]</a></sup> is a real city centre campus, incorporating a boarding school.</p>
<p>Other institutions of higher education in Cambrai are the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_sup%C3%A9rieure_d%27art_de_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École supérieure d'art de Cambrai (page does not exist)">Ecole Supérieure of Art of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89cole_sup%C3%A9rieure_d%27art_de_Cambrai" title="fr:École supérieure d'art de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[72]</a></sup> and the Institute of Nursing Education.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_events_and_festivities">Cultural events and festivities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Cultural events and festivities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 15 August is the communal festival of Cambrai, and one of the highlights of the popular local life. This great festival (or<span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%22ducasse%22" title='fr:"ducasse"'>fr</a>)</span>) extends for ten days in the <i>Place de l'Hôtel de ville</i> [City Hall Square]. The day of 15 August is punctuated by the traditional parade of the giants <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_and_Martine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Martin and Martine (page does not exist)">Martin and Martine</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_et_Martine" title="fr:Martin et Martine">fr</a>)</span>, symbols of the city, and a fireworks display. This festival, originally a procession which took place the day after <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Sunday" title="Trinity Sunday">Trinity Sunday</a>, dates back to 1220. It was embellished over time with fireworks, banquets and cavalcades, and was regarded as one of the seven wonders of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Cambrésis">Cambrésis</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="fr:Cambrésis">fr</a>)</span>. Over the centuries the festival has changed, reflecting the concerns of the contemporary: Since attachment to France it has been celebrated on 15 August, festival of the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Assumption</a>, in response to the wish of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIII_of_France" title="Louis XIII of France">Louis XIII</a> to devote the Kingdom to the Virgin; in 1790 it celebrated the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Rights_of_Man_and_of_the_Citizen" title="Declaration of the Rights of Man and of the Citizen">Declaration of the Rights of Man</a> and the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%AAte_de_la_F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration" title="Fête de la Fédération">Fête de la Fédération</a>; in 1802, with the signature of the <a href="/wiki/Concordat" title="Concordat">concordat</a>, the image of Our Lady of Grace was again carried in procession, reinforced by the bust of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_F%C3%A9nelon" title="François Fénelon">Fénelon</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First Empire</a> it celebrated his Imperial Majesty <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon I</a>. In the 19th century, finally, interests turned more to local life, and the progress of science and industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[a 11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Musically, the town of Cambrai receives two festivals. Firstly, the <i>Juventus</i> classical music festival. The Juventus association mark young talented European soloists. They are appointed, if they accept it, "Juventus Winners" during their first participation in a Juventus festival. Every summer the old and the new winners gather for a fortnight at the festival to prepare chamber music concerts in exceptional conditions. <i>Juventus</i>, established in 1991 at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saltworks_at_Arc-et-Senans" title="Royal Saltworks at Arc-et-Senans">Royal Saltworks at Arc-et-Senans</a>, was set at Cambrai from 1998 with the help of the General Council of the department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[73]</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=BetiZFest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="BetiZFest (page does not exist)"><i>BetiZFest</i></a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/BetiZFest" title="fr:BetiZFest">fr</a>)</span> is an alternative music festival, which has been organised since 2003. It is organised during the month of April. <i>Les Féodales</i> is a street show which represents the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. The last edition took place in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cambrai city hall is the national headquarters of the Union for the horse breed of the "<a href="/wiki/Trait_du_Nord" title="Trait du Nord">Trait du Nord</a>". The Trait du Nord national competition is traditionally held during the last weekend of July at the <i>Palais des Grottes</i>. Bringing together the elite of the breed, it ends on Sunday afternoon on the <i>Place de l’hôtel de Ville</i> with a grand parade, the most important festive presentation in France of a breed of draft horses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Medical density is quite good at Cambrai, when compared with the regional and national averages. In the agglomeration community there are 2.04 general practitioners per 1,000 inhabitants (Nord Pas-de-Calais region and metropolitan France 1.65), and 1.98 specialist doctors per 1,000 inhabitants (region: 1.39, metropolitan France: 1.74).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Saint-Julien hospital, which housed the poor and the sick, was founded in 1070. Today it remains as a chapel adjoining the municipal theatre. Over the following centuries, other hospitals were founded: The Saint-Lazare Hospital for lepers, the Charité Hospital, Saint-Jean Hospital, the Saint Jacques au Bois Hospital to welcome the pilgrims, the general hospice of La Charité founded in 1752 to accommodate the elderly, beggars and the marginalised.</p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> the construction of a modern hospital was envisaged.</p>
<p>The Central Hospital of Cambrai<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[77]</a></sup> has a capacity of 770 beds and 108 seats. It employs a staff of 150 officers and has a non-medical staff of 1,200. Three annexe buildings are reserved for medium and long stay, maternity (1982) and Psychiatry (1983-1884) patients. A Nursing Training Institute was opened in 1967.</p>
<p>The work for the construction of the present site began in 1959, the installation of the patients being carried out between 1966 and 1968. In 2007, the work to modernise and expand the central hospital was undertaken.</p>
<p>The 2010 prize list of "the safest hospitals" places the Central Hospital of Cambrai as the 11th best in the national ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambrai has three private clinics: The Sainte-Marie Clinic, Saint-Roch clinic and the Cambrésis Clinic.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Centre_nautique_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Liberté Swimming Centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai has over a hundred clubs or sporting associations, including the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai_Hockey_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cambrai Hockey Club (page does not exist)">Cambrai Hockey Club</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambrai_Hockey_Club" title="fr:Cambrai Hockey Club">fr</a>)</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[79]</a></sup> playing in the Women's <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> Championship of France, as well as the team of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai_Volley-Ball&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cambrai Volley-Ball (page does not exist)">Cambrai Volley Élan du Cambrésis</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambrai_Volley-Ball" title="fr:Cambrai Volley-Ball">fr</a>)</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[80]</a></sup> which plays in the League (2nd division) and is the only professional club of le Cambrésis.</p>
<p>Facilities include six gymnasiums, two swimming pools, of which the Liberty Swimming Centre was rebuilt and reopened in 2008, the Arsenal de Balagny, which was built between 1581 and 1595, abandoned by the army in 1967 and then rehabilitated as a gym, a leisure centre, a hockey stadium, a rugby stadium and many football pitches, including the Liberty Stadium, home of <a href="/wiki/AC_Cambrai" title="AC Cambrai">AC Cambrai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambrai has a rowing club that goes under the name of <i>Union Nautique de Cambrai</i>. The club is regularly present to the Rowing French Championships. In the early 2000s, one of its feminine team members made it to the World Championships. Since then, the club has been in the phase of beginning a new cycle based on renewed team members, especially youngsters. Every year, the club is home to the Regattas of Cambrai, during which clubs from Northern France gather for sprint-races on a 1000m distance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Billon_(game)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Billon (game) (page does not exist)">billon</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billon_(jeu)" title="fr:Billon (jeu)">fr</a>)</span> is practiced traditionally in regions of Cambrai and Douai.</p>
<p>Cambrai was the departure point for Stage 4 of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Tour_de_France" title="2004 Tour de France">2004 Tour de France</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[83]</a></sup> and once again the departure point of Stage 4 in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Tour_de_France" title="2010 Tour de France">2010 Tour de France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[84]</a></sup> Cambrai is scheduled to host the finish of Stage 4 in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Tour_de_France" title="2015 Tour de France">2015 Tour de France</a>, on 7 July, with a route from <a href="/wiki/Seraing" title="Seraing">Seraing</a>.</p>
<p>In 2010, the newspaper <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%27Equipe" title="L'Equipe">L'Equipe</a></i> ranked Cambrai among the top five cities as the most sporty in France with more than 20,000 inhabitants, along with <a href="/wiki/Lorient" title="Lorient">Lorient</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colmar" title="Colmar">Colmar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antibes" title="Antibes">Antibes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarbes" title="Tarbes">Tarbes</a>. The special prize of "Sport and Disability" was awarded to the city for its access to sport for people with disabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/La_Voix_du_Nord_(daily)" title="La Voix du Nord (daily)">La Voix du Nord</a></i> regional daily publishes a local edition. The <i>L'Observateur du Cambrésis</i> is a weekly local news and announcements. The municipal newspaper <i>Le Cambrésien</i> is distributed in all the mailboxes of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambrai is part of the territory served by radio BLC, a community radio station whose programmes are broadcast from <a href="/wiki/Caudry" title="Caudry">Caudry</a>. The inhabitants of Cambrai also have, in addition to some national radio stations, the programmes of <a href="/wiki/France_Bleu_Nord" title="France Bleu Nord">France Bleu Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A9rie_FM" title="Chérie FM">Chérie FM</a> Cambrai and <a href="/wiki/RFM_(radio)" title="RFM (radio)">RFM Nord</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is covered by the programmes of <a href="/wiki/France_3_Nord-Pas-de-Calais" title="France 3 Nord-Pas-de-Calais">France 3 Nord</a> and the national <a href="/wiki/Television_in_France" title="Television in France">DTT</a> channels. It also received the regional channel of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=W%C3%A9o&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wéo (page does not exist)">Wéo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C3%A9o" title="fr:Wéo">fr</a>)</span>. Oxygen TV is a <a href="/wiki/Web_television" title="Web television">web TV</a> channel "100% of Cambrai" devoted to local information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worship">Worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The people of Cambrai have places of <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> worship.</p>
<p>Cambrai is the seat of a Catholic <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishopric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suffragan_bishop" title="Suffragan bishop">suffragan</a> of Lille since 29 March 2008. Until then, it was the opposite situation with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Cambrai" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cambrai">Archdiocese of Cambrai</a> as the metropolitan archdiocese and Lille and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Arras" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Arras">Arras</a> as its suffragans. The Archdiocese of Cambrai includes the arrondissements of Cambrai, Valenciennes and Avesnes-sur-Helpe. The <a href="/wiki/Deanery" title="Deanery">deanery</a> of Cambrai brings together 13 churches<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[89]</a></sup> grouped into two <a href="/wiki/Parish" title="Parish">parishes</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[90]</a></sup> Our Lady of Grace<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[91]</a></sup> and Saint Vaast-Saint Géry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptist</a> community has an Evangelical Baptist Church,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[93]</a></sup> just as there is a parish of the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_of_France" title="Reformed Church of France">Reformed Church of France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Moroccan cultural and religious association of Cambrai manages the Al Mohssinine <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">Mosque</a> of Escaudain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early 2010, there was no synagogue in Cambrai.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cambrai is the seat of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry_of_the_Cambr%C3%A9sis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chamber of Commerce and Industry of the Cambrésis (page does not exist)">Chamber of Commerce and Industry of the Cambrésis</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chambre_de_commerce_et_d%27industrie_du_Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="fr:Chambre de commerce et d'industrie du Cambrésis">fr</a>)</span>. In April 2007, it decided to merge with the Chamber of Commerce and Industry of Arras, a decision which was called into question on 4 October 2007, by the Ministry of Supervision of the Chambers of Commerce and Industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result of the planned closure in 2012 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Airbase_103_of_Cambrai-Epinoy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Airbase 103 of Cambrai-Epinoy (page does not exist)">Airbase 103 of Cambrai-Epinoy</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_a%C3%A9rienne_103_Cambrai-%C3%89pinoy" title="fr:Base aérienne 103 Cambrai-Épinoy">fr</a>)</span>, Cambrai and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="Cambrésis">Cambrésis</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambr%C3%A9sis" title="fr:Cambrésis">fr</a>)</span> are classified from 1 January 2010 and until 31 December 2012 in the free zone "Zone of Defence Restructuring", allowing enterprises to create, settle or develop tax and social security exemptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_history">Economic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Economic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="525" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg/220px-Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg/330px-Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg/440px-Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sucrerie_escaudoeuvres.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An example of the development of the food industry in the nineteenth century, the <a href="/wiki/Escaud%C5%93uvres" title="Escaudœuvres">Escaudœuvres</a> sugar factory, deemed the largest in Europe</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As early as the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Cambrai was both an agricultural market for its region, which produces mainly cereals and wool, and a centre of weaving (sheets, <a href="/wiki/Isatis_tinctoria" title="Isatis tinctoria">woad</a>, cloth, linen, chiffon). This dual role would persist for a long time. The drapery declined at the end of the 13th century but it was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Batiste" title="Batiste">batiste</a>, a speciality of the city, which experienced its greatest trend in the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[b 32]</a></sup> Production declined, in turn, in the following century, but in 1775 there were still 58,000 pieces of batiste marked to Cambrai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[b 33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Economic activity declined under the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First Empire</a> due to the wars and the British <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a>. In the 19th century the textile industry remained as the dominant activity of the city, with 2,546 workers, men, women and children, in 1848.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HC222_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-HC222-153">[b 34]</a></sup> Batiste made the bulk of Cambrai's trade with other productions such as soap and refined sea salt. The <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food industry</a> grew: Brasserie, chicory; the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%AAtise_de_Cambrai" title="Bêtise de Cambrai">Bêtise de Cambrai</a> was invented in 1850.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HC222_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-HC222-153">[b 34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 19th century the city was industrialised, especially when compared to its neighbours. Municipal officials often refused the installation of new factories, on behalf of sanitation or lack of space. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Sugar_Factory_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Central Sugar Factory of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Central Sugar Factory of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sucrerie_centrale_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Sucrerie centrale de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span> was created in 1872, by Jules Linard<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[98]</a></sup> on the territory of the town of <a href="/wiki/Escaud%C5%93uvres" title="Escaudœuvres">Escaudœuvres</a>. However, according to the census of 1886, industry was supporting more than 9,000 people, while agriculture used only 2,000 at most. The city mainly developed its commercial function: At the beginning of the 20th century the branch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banque_de_France" title="Banque de France">Bank of France</a> from Cambrai ranked 12th in France, before Nice and Toulouse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[b 35]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> reconstruction stimulated the building industry. New enterprises were created from 1950: Hosiery, mechanics and carpentry employed several thousand people, while traditional manufacturing was disappearing: Chicory, chocolate, brewery and weaving. The economic crisis, of the 1970s, seriously degraded the employment situation.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_shops">Business and shops</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Business and shops">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The there are four zones and parks of activity in the agglomeration:</p>
<p>The industrial zone of Cantimpré, to the south-west of the city.</p>
<ul>
<li>The Actipole Park, on the edge of the A2 autoroute 2 kilometres (1.2 mi) west of Cambrai, offers a total area of 97 hectares (240 acres). As it is completely occupied, it is being extended.</li>
<li>The zone of Fontaine-Notre-Dame, a kilometre from the A26 autoroute, offers a total area of 75 hectares (190 acres).</li>
<li>The zone of South Cambrai Proville, one kilometre to the south of Cambrai, on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Route_nationale_44_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Route nationale 44 (France) (page does not exist)">RN 44</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_nationale_44_(France)" title="fr:Route nationale 44 (France)">fr</a>)</span>, in the direction of Saint-Quentin, is devoted to the commercial areas over an area of 40 hectares (99 acres).</li>
</ul>
<p>The economy of Cambrai is based on four pillars:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a>, which occupies a third of the territory of the commune.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Agribusiness" title="Agribusiness">agri-food industry</a>, which occupies an important place in the economy of the commune (confectionery, candy, dairy, etc.) due to strong agricultural activity (<a href="/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">intensive farming</a> of <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">livestock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereals</a>) in the arrondissement (80% of the area).</li>
<li>Logistics, benefitting from the situation of the commune of Cambrai in the heart of the triangle London-Paris-Benelux and the intersection of two motorways, tends to be concentrated in the western part of the agglomeration. Thus all of the 97 hectares (240 acres) of the Actipôle Raillencourt zone of activity located 2 kilometres (1.2 mi) west of Cambrai on the edge of the A2 autoroute are now used, partly by distribution undertakings, for a thousand jobs around. The extensions Actipole 2 and 3 are underway or study.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">Textile</a>, found predominantly in the rest of the arrondissement (<a href="/wiki/Caudry" title="Caudry">Caudry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villers-Outr%C3%A9aux" title="Villers-Outréaux">Villers-Outréaux</a>, etc.) is represented in Cambrai by clothing and linens. The Cambrai region is associated with those of <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_Community_of_Lille_M%C3%A9tropole" title="Urban Community of Lille Métropole">Lille Urban Community</a> within the Up-Tex <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=P%C3%B4le_de_comp%C3%A9titivit%C3%A9_en_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pôle de compétitivité en France (page does not exist)">competitiveness cluster</a>, specialised in textile products high performance and customisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[99]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The Central Hospital of Cambrai, the commune of Cambrai, <a href="/wiki/Auchan" title="Auchan">Auchan</a>, Les Papillons blancs, <a href="/wiki/Cora_(hypermarket)" title="Cora (hypermarket)">Cora</a>, TANIS (chemistry, rubber, plastic), the <i>Compagnie des Engrenages et Réducteurs Messiaen Durand</i> (mechanical equipment) and the departmental fire and rescue service were, in order, the eight major employers in the town, in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Perspectives">Perspectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Perspectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The future <a href="/wiki/Seine%E2%80%93Nord_Europe_Canal" title="Seine–Nord Europe Canal">Seine-Scheldt link</a>, the commissioning of which is scheduled for 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[101]</a></sup> is today one of the most promising elements of economic development to the city and the area of Cambrai. The <a href="/wiki/Combined_transport" title="Combined transport">multimodal</a> platform of activities of <a href="/wiki/Marquion" title="Marquion">Marquion</a>, 10 kilometres (6.2 mi) west of Cambrai and on 156 hectares (390 acres), should be employed to host European logistics and distribution centres and agro-food industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_of_the_population_and_taxation">Income of the population and taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Income of the population and taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, the median <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Revenu_fiscal_par_m%C3%A9nage_en_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Revenu fiscal par ménage en France (page does not exist)">taxable household income</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revenu_fiscal_par_m%C3%A9nage_en_France" title="fr:Revenu fiscal par ménage en France">fr</a>)</span> was €15,302, which ranks Cambrai at 25,917th place among the 31,604 communes with more than 50 households in metropolitan France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, 263 Cambrai tax households performed the <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_tax_on_wealth" title="Solidarity tax on wealth">solidarity tax on wealth</a>, for a mean wealth of €1.665 million and an average tax amount of €5,017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the results of the 2006 Census,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSEEemploi_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-INSEEemploi-162">[105]</a></sup> the economically <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">active population</a> aged 15 and over of the commune included 14,597 people, 18.4% were <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployed</a> (France: 11.5%) and 81.6% were employed (France: 88.5%). Among the unemployed, most affected were "less than 20 years" (44.39%) and "20-24 years" (31.81%).</p>
<p>The distribution of jobs by <a href="/wiki/Business_sector" title="Business sector">sector of activity</a> shows the predominant weight (more than 80%) of the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector</a>. This distribution reflects the role which the administrative and commercial centre plays in the commune for the surrounding countryside.</p>

<p>The journeys to work are mostly by car (73.93%, France 70.2%) and one can note the low weight of transport (4.57 per cent against an average of 13.53% in France).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_culture_and_heritage">Local culture and heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Local culture and heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sites_and_monuments">Sites and monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Sites and monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_monuments_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of historic monuments of Cambrai (page does not exist)">List of historic monuments of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liste_des_monuments_historiques_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Liste des monuments historiques de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG/220px-Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG/330px-Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG/440px-Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambrai_Porte_Notre-Dame.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Notre-Dame Gate (1634)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A large part of the monumental heritage of Cambrai has disappeared over the centuries. It was firstly <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, in order to build a citadel at the Mont-des-Bœufs, who ordered the destruction of the Abbey Saint-Gery of Gothic style in 1543.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> all of the religious buildings of the town were sold as national property and destroyed, including the <a href="/wiki/Old_Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Old Cambrai Cathedral">old cathedral</a>. Only four churches, a converted attic, a hospital, a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_of_reason&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Temple of reason (page does not exist)">Temple of reason</a> and a prison, were spared.</p>
<p>The dismantling of the fortifications, from 1894, led to the disappearance of many <a href="/wiki/City_gate" title="City gate">gates</a>. Some have been preserved thanks to the interventions of the Society of Emulation of the city.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> was again responsible for significant destruction, the German army undermined and torched the city centre before retirement in September 1918: A total of 1,214 buildings are destroyed, including the city hall which was rebuilt in <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> style before the Revolution by the architects <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Denis_Antoine" title="Jacques Denis Antoine">Jacques Denis Antoine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicolas-Henri_Jardin" title="Nicolas-Henri Jardin">Nicolas-Henri Jardin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[a 12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, in April 1944, and then again in May, July and until 11 August, Cambrai suffered Allied bombardments: A total of 55% of the buildings were heavily damaged and 13% were completely destroyed.</p>
<p>Despite this considerable destruction, the city kept an important monumental heritage. Cambrai has been classified as a <a href="/wiki/French_Towns_and_Lands_of_Art_and_History" title="French Towns and Lands of Art and History">City of Art and History</a> since 1992, the first town of the Nord department to obtain this prestigious label.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_heritage">Religious heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Religious heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cath%C3%A9drale_Notre-Dame_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Cathedral of Our Lady</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Cambrai Cathedral">Our Lady of Grace Cathedral</a>, completed in 1703 in the classical style of the time, replaced the admirable <a href="/wiki/Old_Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Old Cambrai Cathedral">Gothic Cathedral</a> from the 12th century after the Revolution of 1789. There is no trace on the present <i>Place Fénelon</i> of the former building. The apse contains the monumental tomb of Fénelon, a masterpiece of the sculptor <a href="/wiki/David_d%27Angers" title="David d'Angers">David d'Angers</a>, and the semitransepts with <i>l'Icône Notre Dame de Grâce</i> [the Icon of Our Lady of Grace] and the nine reputed <a href="/wiki/Grisaille" title="Grisaille">grisailles</a> by <a href="/wiki/Marten_Jozef_Geeraerts" title="Marten Jozef Geeraerts">Geeraerts</a> of Antwerp. The grand <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)#Church_organs" title="Organ (music)">organs</a> were built by the house of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Schyven&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Schyven (page does not exist)">Pierre Schyven</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Schyven" title="fr:Pierre Schyven">fr</a>)</span> of Ixelles in 1897. After the events of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, extensive restoration was undertaken by the organ builder Auguste Convers, who brought the current instrument to 49 stops with 3,670 pipes. The building was classified in the inventory of <a href="/wiki/Monument_historique" title="Monument historique">Historic Monuments</a> on 9 August 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Seminary_Chapel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grand Seminary Chapel (page does not exist)">Grand Seminary Chapel</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chapelle_des_J%C3%A9suites_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Chapelle des Jésuites de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span> most commonly called the College of the Jesuits' Chapel, completed in 1692, is a unique example of <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> art in France, to the north of Paris. The chapel served as a prison to the nearby Revolutionary Court in 1794, and it was classified in the inventory of Historic Monuments on 30 April 1920.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89glise_Saint-G%C3%A9ry_de_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Église Saint-Géry de Cambrai (page does not exist)">Church of Saint-Géry</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89glise_Saint-G%C3%A9ry_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Église Saint-Géry de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, a listed historical monument since 26 November 1919,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[109]</a></sup> is one of the oldest monuments of Cambrai. It contains a remarkable <a href="/wiki/Rood_screen" title="Rood screen">choir screen</a> in polychromatic marble carved by the Cambrai native <a href="/wiki/Gaspard_and_Balthazard_Marsy" title="Gaspard and Balthazard Marsy">Gaspard Marsy</a> as well as <i>La mise au tombeauu</i> by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Peter Paul Rubens</a> dating from 1616. The grand organs built in 1867 by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Merklin" title="Joseph Merklin">Merklin</a> were the subject of a significant transformation in 1978. The current instrument has 41 stops. This church has been the subject of a restoration of the frontage and roofing over a period of four years (2011-2015).</p>
<p>Other buildings of Cambrai are also classified or listed as Historic Monuments. The former <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Convent_of_the_Recollects_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Convent of the Recollects of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Convent of the Recollects</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Couvent_des_R%C3%A9collets_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Couvent des Récollets de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span> has been registered since 2 March 1943,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[110]</a></sup> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=B%C3%A9guinages_Saint-Vaast_and_Saint-Nicolas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Béguinages Saint-Vaast and Saint-Nicolas (page does not exist)">Béguinages Saint-Vaast and Saint-Nicolas</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A9guinages_Saint-Vaast_et_Saint-Nicolas" title="fr:Béguinages Saint-Vaast et Saint-Nicolas">fr</a>)</span> have been classified as Historic Monuments since 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_heritage">Military heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Military heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Citadel: Despite its dismantling in the 19th century, the Citadel of Charles V retained the counter-mine galleries which are today buried; the Royal gate and drawbridge, classified in the inventory of historical monuments on 14 April 1932,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[112]</a></sup> flanked on the back of two guardhouses and an arsenal of the 16th century. Among subsequent developments, a powder magazine, housing for officers and a "bombproof" barracks of the 19th century are also noteworthy.</p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Château de Selles (page does not exist)">Château de Selles</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Selles" title="fr:Château de Selles">fr</a>)</span> is an old fortified château, which was built in the 11th century. Once isolated by the waters of the Scheldt, it has retained its towers and walls and especially buried ducts. The ducts include much graffiti which attests to the desperation of the prisoners, confined on the orders of the Count-Bishop.</p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Porte_de_Paris_(Cambrai)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Porte de Paris (Cambrai) (page does not exist)">Portes de Paris</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porte_de_Paris_(Cambrai)" title="fr:Porte de Paris (Cambrai)">fr</a>)</span> (late 14th century),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[113]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Porte_Notre-Dame_(Cambrai)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Porte Notre-Dame (Cambrai) (page does not exist)">Notre Dame</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porte_Notre-Dame_(Cambrai)" title="fr:Porte Notre-Dame (Cambrai)">fr</a>)</span> (17th century)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[114]</a></sup> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tour_Saint-Fiacre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tour Saint-Fiacre (page does not exist)">Tours des Sottes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tour_Saint-Fiacre" title="fr:Tour Saint-Fiacre">fr</a>)</span> (or Saint-Fiacre),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[115]</a></sup> the Caudron (1st half of the 15th century)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[116]</a></sup> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tour_des_Arquets&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tour des Arquets (page does not exist)">Arquets</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tour_des_Arquets" title="fr:Tour des Arquets">fr</a>)</span> (16th century)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[117]</a></sup> are the remains of the medieval walls.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_heritage">Civil heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Civil heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carillon-Cambrai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="328" height="335" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Carillon-Cambrai.jpg/220px-Carillon-Cambrai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/12/Carillon-Cambrai.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carillon-Cambrai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Martin and Martine strike the hours in the bell tower of Cambrai's town hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Belfry_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Belfry of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Belfry of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beffroi_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Beffroi de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, formerly the bell tower of the Church of Saint-Martin. The monument, built in the 15th century, became a belfry of Cambrai in 1550. Classified in the inventory of historical monuments on 15 July 1965,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[118]</a></sup> this building was inscribed by UNESCO, within a group of 23 in the north of France, as an extension of the 30 Belgian belfries inscribed in 1999 under the name of "Belfries of Flanders and Wallonia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city hall, renovated in 1932, opens onto the <i>Grand'Place</i> by a majestic Greek-style façade, surmounted by a bell tower where two bronze bell ringers, giant and Moorish type, strike the hours on a big bell above the big clock: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_and_Martine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Martin and Martine (page does not exist)">Martin and Martine</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_et_Martine" title="fr:Martin et Martine">fr</a>)</span>, the protectors of the city. The marriage hall contains a series of frescoes and can be visited on request.</p>
<p>The Hotel de Francqueville (18th century) houses the rich collections of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Museum_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Museum of Cambrai (page does not exist)">Museum of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Musée de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, considerably enlarged and renovated in 1994. The relief map of the city, as it was at the end of the 17th century, is the starting point for essential guided tours of the city.</p>
<p>The <i>Maison Espagnole</i> [Spanish House], headquarters of the Tourist Office, dates from 1595 and is the last house which is half-timbered and gabled on regional-style street. Oak sculptures (<a href="/wiki/Chimera_(mythology)" title="Chimera (mythology)">chimeras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caryatid" title="Caryatid">caryatids</a>) which adorned its façade in the 19th century are exposed on the first floor inside after undergoing a serious restoration. One can visit its medieval cellars. This building has been classified in the inventory of historical monuments on 31 August 1920.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1360" data-file-width="2048" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG/220px-March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG/330px-March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG/440px-March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:March%C3%A9_couvert_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The covered market</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The covered market, built after World War II, is home to lively Les Halles market days.</p>
<p>The subterranean space<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[a 13]</a></sup> which extends below the centre of the city, as in other medieval cities, was explored in the middle of the 19th century as well as to the end of the 20th century. Carved into the white chalk, they include galleries, Romanesque and Gothic vaulted rooms. There are also wells, niches for statues. These excavations have served as quarries for the extraction of materials of construction, as well as stone for lime: The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Catiche&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Catiche (page does not exist)">"catiches"</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catiche" title="fr:Catiche">fr</a>)</span> [underground quarries] are inverted funnels about 15 metres (49 ft) deep and 10–12 metres (33–39 ft) wide at the base. This underground space was also used, until 1944, for shelters and caches during sieges, invasion or bombing. Their dating is uncertain: It is not impossible that some of these excavations were carved during the Roman era, but it is likely that they were spaced out over a long period, according to the needs. Tours are organised by the tourist office.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorial_heritage">Memorial heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Memorial heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The German military cemetery of the <i>Route de Solesmes</i> and Cambrai East Military Cemetery: The cemetery and the <i>Route de Solesmes</i> was created by the German army in March 1917. Occupied since 1914, Cambrai was an important centre of command, logistics and health for the occupant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[121]</a></sup> The cemetery was opened to accommodate the bodies of soldiers who died in hospitals in the city, including at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1917)" title="Battle of Arras (1917)">Battle of Arras</a> (April–May 1917) and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1917)" title="Battle of Cambrai (1917)">Battle of Cambrai</a> (November–December 1917). The cemetery currently has 10,685 German graves, as well as those of 192 Russian prisoners of war and six Romanians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[122]</a></sup> Two spaces, forming the Cambrai East Military Cemetery, contain the graves of 501 soldiers of the British Imperial Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_heritage">Environmental heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Environmental heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1360" data-file-width="2048" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kiosque_%C3%A0_musique_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The bandstand is one of the oldest in France</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cambrai has the label "Floral City" with three flowers awarded by the <i>National Council of Floral Cities and Villages of France</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Concours_des_villes_et_villages_fleuris" title="Concours des villes et villages fleuris">Foral Competition of Cities and Villages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The current public garden dates from the 19th century, which saw the creation of green spaces in the middle to encourage <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygienics</a> and which were liberated in addition to the areas occupied by the fortifications. This garden, divided into three distinct but contiguous parts, is located on the site of the old fortifications that surrounded the citadel built under <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>:</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grottes_Jardin_public_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "caves" of the public garden</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The "flower garden", designed by the landscape architect <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Barillet-Deschamps" title="Jean-Pierre Barillet-Deschamps">Jean-Pierre Barillet-Deschamps</a>, was established between 1852 and 1865 on 6 hectares (15 acres). This garden was originally the only one planned but, at the insistence of the prefect of the time, it was increased to 9 hectares (22 acres) in 1864.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[a 14]</a></sup></li>
<li>The "Monstrelet Garden" designed "in English", was soon added to the previous. It is so called because it houses a statue of <a href="/wiki/Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet" title="Enguerrand de Monstrelet">Enguerrand de Monstrelet</a>, chronicler of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> who was the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pr%C3%A9v%C3%B4t_(Ancien_R%C3%A9gime)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prévôt (Ancien Régime) (page does not exist)">Provost</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pr%C3%A9v%C3%B4t_(Ancien_R%C3%A9gime)" title="fr:Prévôt (Ancien Régime)">fr</a>)</span> of Cambrai. In 1876, the bandstand was erected, built on the plans of André de Baralle.</li>
<li>The "garden of caves", built in the early 19th century, carries a total area of more than 15 hectares (37 acres). The "caves", decorated with a waterfall, were the main attraction and gave their name to this part of the garden. They were completed in 1906 and in 2010 are awaiting rehabilitation.</li>
</ul>
<p>These gardens, and in particular their statues, were damaged by the two world wars. In 1972, a modern hall, named as the <i>Palais des Grottes</i> [Mansion of Caves] and hosting exhibitions, trade fairs and concerts, was built in the middle of the garden of the same name.</p>
<p>A few other squares or gardens complement the green spaces of Cambrai: Fenelon Square, established in 1861 to the designs of Barillet-Deschamps on the site of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Old Cambrai Cathedral">ancient metropolis</a> and decorated in 1864 with a water fountain, that of the <i>Place Marcelin Berthelot</i>, which dates from 1911. This is at the foot of the walls of the Château de Selles, dating from the same year. The one of the Arquets tower dates from 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[c 4]</a></sup> The avenues and boulevards planted with trees and flowers to complete make Cambrai a "green" city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_heritage">Cultural heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Cultural heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG/220px-Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG/330px-Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG/440px-Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Cambrai.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The theatre of Cambrai, between the National Conservatory of Music and Dramatic Art and the chapel of the old Saint-Julien Hospital</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mus%C3%A9e_de_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Musée de Cambrai (page does not exist)">Musée des beaux-arts of Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Musée de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, opened in 1847 to present revolutionary seizures, has been installed since 1893 in a mansion of the 18th century, the Hotel de Francqueville. Renovated in 1994, it has three departments (archaeology, fine arts and heritage of Cambrai) on 4,300 square metres (46,000 sq ft) of which the most important is that of art. It presents Flemish and Dutch paintings from the 17th century and French artists of the 19th and 20th century. A recent donation also allowed it to present a collection of geometric <a href="/wiki/Abstraction_(art)" title="Abstraction (art)">abstractions</a> of the second half of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Diocesan Museum of Sacred Art still officially retains its label <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mus%C3%A9e_de_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Musée de France (page does not exist)">"Musée de France"</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_France" title="fr:Musée de France">fr</a>)</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[note 6]</a></sup> although it was closed to the public in 1975. This private museum is managed by the diocese, which is looking for ways to reopen the collections to the public. The items of this collection may be the subject of loans for temporary exhibitions and include objects from the archaeological excavations of the city of Cambrai, architectural elements, sculpture, paintings, pieces of jewellery and liturgical ornaments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[126]</a></sup> This museum's history began in 1926 when Monseignor <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean-Arthur_Chollet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean-Arthur Chollet (page does not exist)">Chollet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Arthur_Chollet" title="fr:Jean-Arthur Chollet">fr</a>)</span>, Archbishop of Cambrai, established a commission of religious history and sacred art aimed to inventory and preserve the archives and movable heritage of the diocese. Canon Cyrille Thelliez became secretary. In 1958, many religious objects from the diocese were gathered together and Thelliez founded the Diocesan Museum, the first religious art museum opened in France. The museum was installed in the former chapel of the Grand Seminary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Théâtre de Cambrai was built in 1924 by the architect <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Leprince-Ringuet (page does not exist)">Pierre Leprince-Ringuet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet" title="fr:Pierre Leprince-Ringuet">fr</a>)</span>, on the site of a chapel of the 16th century which was destroyed during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. The chapel had been abandoned for 25 years when its rehabilitation was undertaken in 1999. The renovated theatre was inaugurated in 2003. It is an Italian theatre of 700 seats which hosts various performances, including those of the <i>Scènes mitoyennes</i> [Adjoining Stages] association and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Festival_Juventus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Festival Juventus (page does not exist)">Juventus classical music festival</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Festival_Juventus" title="fr:Festival Juventus">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<p>The <i>Palais des grottes</i> [Mansion of Caves] situated in the public garden, is a large multi-purpose hall with a capacity of 1,500 people and which can accommodate concerts, (including the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=BetiZFest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="BetiZFest (page does not exist)">BetiZFest</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/BetiZFest" title="fr:BetiZFest">fr</a>)</span>), fairs or exhibitions. Its remarkable roof shape, formed of a <a href="/wiki/Paraboloid" title="Paraboloid">hyperbolic paraboloid</a> (or "saddle"), was built in 1974 by then-advanced techniques and demonstrates a concrete form of architecture in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[a 15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The media library is a classified municipal library:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[128]</a></sup> It has an important old <a href="/wiki/Fonds" title="Fonds">fonds</a>, with 956 manuscripts, the oldest dating back to the 7th century, from the confiscations made during the revolutionary era to religious communities, very important in the city, and emigrants of the region. This fonds was subsequently enriched by gifts, bequests and purchases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[129]</a></sup> In 1975, it was one of the first institutions to adopt the title of "media library". It is divided into four services: Youth, adults, library and local history and old books.</p>
<p>Cambrai has a national school of music and dramatic arts<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[130]</a></sup> which obtained the <i>Conservatoire à rayonnement départemental</i> label in 2007.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personalities_linked_to_the_commune">Personalities linked to the commune</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Personalities linked to the commune">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Dubois" title="Guillaume Dubois">Guillaume Dubois</a> (c. 1656–1723), known as Cardinal Dubois. appointed Archbishop of Cambrai, though never set foot there</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Defr%C3%A9mery" title="Charles Defrémery">Charles Defrémery</a> (1822–1883), orientalist born in Cambrai</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Marcel_Lermoyez" title="Marcel Lermoyez">Marcel Lermoyez</a> (1858–1929), otologist</li>

<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Leprince-Ringuet (page does not exist)">Pierre Leprince-Ringuet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Leprince-Ringuet" title="fr:Pierre Leprince-Ringuet">fr</a>)</span> (c. 1874–1954), architect of the reconstruction after World War II</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henri_de_Lubac" title="Henri de Lubac">Henri de Lubac</a> (1896–1991), born in Cambrai, Jesuit Catholic theologian and Bishop</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Julien_Torma" title="Julien Torma">Julien Torma</a> (1902–1933), writer, playwright and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Dumont" title="René Dumont">René Dumont</a> (1904–2001), born in Cambrai, engineer in <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_science" title="Agricultural science">agronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociologist</a>, and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Political_ecology" title="Political ecology">political ecology</a></li>
