<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary_specialities">Culinary specialities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Culinary specialities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1221" data-file-width="1864" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg/220px-B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg/330px-B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg/440px-B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B%C3%AAtises_de_Cambrai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bêtises de Cambrai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The two best-known gastronomic specialties of Cambrai are the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Andouillette_de_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Andouillette de Cambrai (page does not exist)">Andouillette de Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andouillette_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Andouillette de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, a sausage traditionally made of ground veal (which is now prohibited by European regulations), whose associated gastronomic society is one of the most representative in the region, and the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%AAtise_de_Cambrai" title="Bêtise de Cambrai">Bêtise de Cambrai</a>, a coated mint confection which is one of the most emblematic gourmet specialties of France.</p>
<p>The gastronomy of Cambrai also accounts for other less known specialities: Tripe, liver pâté with plums, hare with grapes, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hochepot&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hochepot (page does not exist)">hochepot</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/hochepot" title="fr:hochepot">fr</a>)</span> of <a href="/wiki/Partridge" title="Partridge">partridge</a> with puréed lentils, but also the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boulette_de_Cambrai" title="Boulette de Cambrai">Boulette de Cambrai</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boulette_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Boulette de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, <a href="/wiki/Fromage_blanc" title="Fromage blanc">fromage blanc</a> with fine herbs, and also a cheese <a href="/wiki/Trademark" title="Trademark">trademarked</a> as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tome_de_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tome de Cambrai (page does not exist)">"Tome de Cambrai"</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tome_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Tome de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, or even crackers and <i>pain crotté</i> [muddy bread] (a type of <a href="/wiki/French_toast" title="French toast">French toast</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heraldry.2C_motto">Heraldry, motto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Heraldry, motto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;padding:5px 8px;width:120px;">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blason_cambrai.svg" title="Arms of Cambrai"><img alt="Arms of Cambrai" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="600" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Blason_cambrai.svg/120px-Blason_cambrai.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Blason_cambrai.svg/180px-Blason_cambrai.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Blason_cambrai.svg/240px-Blason_cambrai.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a></div>
</div>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;">The arms of Cambrai are <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazoned</a>:<br/>
<i>"Or, a double-headed eagle sable, (haloed) beaked and membered gules, overall an inescutcheon Or, 3 lions azure."</i><br/>
<br/>
The first known arms appear on a seal from 1340. They represented an eagle holding in its talons the arms of le Cambrésis, <i>"of Or three Lion Cubs of azure"</i>. Under the Spanish domination these arms were slightly modified, the double-headed eagle of the Holy Roman Empire became an honourable figure<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[note 7]</a></sup> and arms of the Cambrésis being removed. The coat of arms thus means "Cambrai city of the empire and capital of the Cambrésis".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[131]</a></sup>
<p><br/></p>
<p><br/></p>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;padding:5px 8px;width:120px;">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png"><img alt="Blason Cambrai chambre de commerce.png" data-file-height="407" data-file-width="365" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png/120px-Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png/180px-Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png/240px-Blason_Cambrai_chambre_de_commerce.png 2x" width="120"/></a></div>
</div>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;">The eagle is usually surmounted with the ducal crown, the city having been elevated to a Duchy in 1510. In 1815 Cambrai received from <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France" title="Louis XVIII of France">Louis XVIII</a> the right again to its ancient arms. In 1919, it was awarded the cross of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a>, and in 1945 the <a href="/wiki/Croix_de_guerre_1939%E2%80%931945_(France)" title="Croix de guerre 1939–1945 (France)">Croix de Guerre</a>.<br/>
<br/>
On the front of the Chamber of Commerce (shown adjoining), built after the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the arms are surmounted by the Ducal Crown, framed by the giants <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_and_Martine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Martin and Martine (page does not exist)">Martin and Martine</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_et_Martine" title="fr:Martin et Martine">fr</a>)</span>, and increased by the cross of the Legion of Honour.
<p><br/></p>
<p><br/></p>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The motto of the city has changed several times:</p>
<ul>
<li>1579: <i>"Cambray, city of peace."</i></li>
<li>1580: <i>"Concordia parvæ res crescunt"</i> ("Harmony makes small things grow"). This motto is the same as that of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a> (<i>"<a href="/wiki/Unity_makes_strength" title="Unity makes strength">Unity makes strength</a>"</i>)</li>
<li>Current motto: <i>"Proud of its past, sure of its future."</i></li>
</ul>
<p>The logo of the city is a stylisation of the steeples of the <a href="/wiki/Cambrai_Cathedral" title="Cambrai Cathedral">cathedral</a>, the Saint-Géry Church and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Belfry_of_Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Belfry of Cambrai (page does not exist)">belfry</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beffroi_de_Cambrai" title="fr:Beffroi de Cambrai">fr</a>)</span>, a visual signature of the city, visible from afar. Locally, Cambrai is known as "the city of three spires".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_life">Military life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Military life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1711-1712, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, the regiments of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roussillon_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roussillon Regiment (page does not exist)">Rousillon</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9giment_de_Roussillon" title="fr:Régiment de Roussillon">fr</a>)</span> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%A9giment_Royal-Comtois" title="Régiment Royal-Comtois">Royal-Comtois</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9giment_Royal-Comtois" title="fr:Régiment Royal-Comtois">fr</a>)</span> had their barracks at Cambrai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the late 19th century, two military units were stationed at Cambrai. The <a href="/wiki/1st_Infantry_Regiment_(France)" title="1st Infantry Regiment (France)">1st Infantry Regiment</a> was quartered at Cambrai from 1870 to 1914, when it left for Belgium, before returning in 1919. It was split between the citadel and the Renel barracks. In 1940 it was again sent to Belgium, before being dissolved in 1942 in the free zone and did not return to Cambrai. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=4th_Cuirassier_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="4th Cuirassier Regiment (page does not exist)">4th Cuirassier Regiment</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/4e_r%C3%A9giment_de_cuirassiers_(France)" title="fr:4e régiment de cuirassiers (France)">fr</a>)</span> arrived in Cambrai in 1889 and is the Mortier quarter. This regiment was dissolved at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> the Mortier quarter was assigned to the Selection Centre No. 2, today disbanded.</p>
<p>Until 2012, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Airbase_103_Cambrai-%C3%89pinoy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Airbase 103 Cambrai-Épinoy (page does not exist)">Airbase 103</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_a%C3%A9rienne_103_Cambrai-%C3%89pinoy" title="fr:Base aérienne 103 Cambrai-Épinoy">fr</a>)</span> "<a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Mouchotte" title="René Mouchotte">René Mouchotte</a>" was near the city, founded in 1953 and which hosted the 01.012 Fighter Squadron "Cambrésis" created in 1952, the 02.012 "Picardy" and the 03.012 "Cornouailles" [Cornwall], as well as a ground-to-air defence squadron.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambrai_in_literature_and_cinema">Cambrai in literature and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Cambrai in literature and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_J%C3%BCnger" title="Ernst Jünger">Ernst Jünger</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Storm_of_Steel" title="Storm of Steel">Storm of Steel</a></i>, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, described Cambrai in 1917:</li>
</ul>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Cambrai is a small, quiet and sleepy city of Artois (sic), to the name of which is attached many historical memories. Narrow and antiquated alleys run like a maze around the huge city hall, doors eaten away by the centuries and many churches, the largest of which saw Fénelon preach. Heavy steeples stand amongst a jumble of pointed gables. Broad avenues lead to a well-kept public garden, which is adorned with a monument to Louis Blériot.
<p>The inhabitants are peaceful and cordial people, who lead in their big houses, simple in appearance, but richly furnished, with a life of wellbeing. The small city has been rightfully nicknamed "the city of millionaires" because, just before the war, there were forty of these <a href="/wiki/Croesus" title="Croesus">Croesus</a>-like people.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">Great War</a> tore this hole of the province in its sleep of Sleeping Beauty and the gigantic turn of home struggles...</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; text-align: right;"><cite>— <a href="/wiki/Ernst_J%C3%BCnger" title="Ernst Jünger">Ernst Jünger</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Storm_of_Steel" title="Storm of Steel">Storm of Steel</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[133]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<ul>
<li>The streets of Cambrai served as a backgrop to <i>Sang noir</i> [Black Blood], a 90-minute fiction filmed from 7 March to 6 April 2006 through Production of <a href="/wiki/France_3" title="France 3">France 3</a> Lille, based on the novel of the same name by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Guilloux" title="Louis Guilloux">Louis Guilloux</a> which takes place in 1917 in a small town, far from the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a>.</li>
<li>In 2007, the construction of the bypass of Cambrai was used for the filming of the movie <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Beginning_(2009_film)" title="In the Beginning (2009 film)">In the Beginning</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Giannoli" title="Xavier Giannoli">Xavier Giannoli</a>. Some scenes of the film <i>Présumé coupable</i> [Presumed Guilty], by Vincent Garenq, were shot at Cambrai in April 2010.</li>
<li>The comic book <i><a href="/wiki/Asterix_and_the_Banquet" title="Asterix and the Banquet">Asterix and the Banquet</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Goscinny" title="René Goscinny">Goscinny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Uderzo" title="Albert Uderzo">Uderzo</a> have a journey to various cities in Roman Gaul, including <i>Camaracum</i> (Cambrai): <a href="/wiki/Asterix_(character)" title="Asterix (character)">Asterix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obelix" title="Obelix">Obelix</a> buy <a href="/wiki/B%C3%AAtise_de_Cambrai" title="Bêtise de Cambrai">bêtises</a>.</li>
<li>The young-adult novel <i>Les Bêtises de Cambrai</i> (Airvey, 2011) by Eric Callens.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambrai_and_philately">Cambrai and philately</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambrai&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Cambrai and philately">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Four postage stamps have been issued in connection with the city of Cambrai:</p>
<ul>
<li>10 July 1947, a stamp commemorating <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_F%C3%A9nelon" title="François Fénelon">Fénelon</a>, Archbishop of Cambrai, with a face value of 4.50 <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">Francs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>19 February 1972, a stamp commemorating <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bl%C3%A9riot" title="Louis Blériot">Louis Blériot</a>, born in Cambrai, with a face value of 0.50 Francs with surcharge: 0.10 Francs for the benefit of the French Red Cross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li>14 May 1977, a stamp commemorating the capture of Cambrai in 1677 and the annexation of Cambrésis by France, with a face value of 0.80 Francs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[136]</a></sup></li>
<li>25 July 2009, a stamp commemorating the crossing of the English channel by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bl%C3%A9riot" title="Louis Blériot">Louis Blériot</a>, with a face value of €2.00.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[137]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
